Second Sheet

Current Commentary

The Attitudes of the U.S. and France Towards the German Question

The most important issue in the international community is the war debt and reparations problem. The world is paying attention to the attitudes of the U.S. and French governments, as the lack of resolution of this issue prevents the clearing of international opinions. The most affected parties are Germany, the U.S., and France. Today, the German Center Party issued a notice hoping for a swift resolution to the reparations problem, stating that resolving this issue is the way to avoid revolutionary suffering in Germany and throughout Europe. It is also hoped that all rational people in the world will take precautions to avoid future regrets. The urgency and alarm in their words are evident.

Regarding the attitudes of the U.S. and France, although there has been no formal expression, judging from the declarations of U.S. Undersecretary of State Carr and French Foreign Minister Briand, there is hope that the problem can be resolved. Carr stated that the U.S. government does not insist on a complete separation of reparations and war debts and will consider whether to temporarily change its policy if necessary. German newspapers have emphasized his declaration, stating that it is sufficient to increase the political significance of the U.S. to Germany. Briand said that his efforts to maintain peace are due to France being suspected of disrupting peace, which he must overcome all difficulties to prevent. He also said that the misunderstandings between Germany and France in recent years can be eliminated in the near future. Although the reparations problem was not explicitly mentioned, it is easy to see between the lines that the reparations problem is approachable. Therefore, I believe that these messages are worthy of the world's attention.

Foreign Dispatches

Germany's Center Party Continues to Trust the Government

Reparations Create an Economic Crisis

Hoping the World Will Rise Up to Salvage the Situation

Berlin, 14th (National News Agency) – The German Center Party's Executive Committee and its parliamentary group held a closed-door meeting today. Those hoping to hear a speech from Brüning were disappointed. However, after the meeting, the party issued a statement expressing its continued trust in the government and hoped for a swift resolution to the reparations issue. It stated that resolving this issue is essential to prevent revolution and suffering in Germany and throughout Europe. It further hoped that people of reason worldwide would take preventative measures to avoid the regret of being unable to salvage the situation.

Berlin, 14th (National News Agency) – U.S. Undersecretary of State Castle recently declared that the U.S. government does not insist on a complete separation between reparations and war debts, and that the U.S. government is willing to reconsider whether its policies should be changed if necessary. This declaration is highly valued in political and opinion circles here because it has increased the political significance of the upcoming visit to Germany by U.S. Secretary of State Stimson and Treasury Secretary Mellon. The value of this declaration for Germany will soon be discovered, but it does not imply that the United States is prepared to allow the suspension of war debt payments.

Briand Reaffirms Maintaining Peace

Misunderstandings with Germany Can Be Easily Resolved

Paris, 14th (National News Agency) – Today, Foreign Minister Briand spoke at a banquet for veterans of the European War, saying that he intends to continue shouldering the heavy responsibility of diplomacy for the sake of world peace. Therefore, the honor bestowed upon him by the veterans is an endorsement of his peace policy. He is striving to maintain peace because France is suspected of disrupting it, so he must overcome all difficulties to dispel the world's doubts. He then spoke of Franco-German relations, saying that misunderstandings between the two countries in recent years can be resolved in the near future.

French Excursion Ship Capsizes

Encountering Storm on Return Trip from Picnic

Over Four Hundred Drowned

Saint-Nazaire, 14th (National News Agency) – The French excursion ship Saint-Philibert, carrying 600 passengers, departed from Nantes this morning for a picnic on the island of Noirmoutier. This afternoon, while returning from the island, five miles offshore from here, a large storm arose. Passengers, witnessing a giant wave approaching, panicked and rushed to one side of the ship. The ship's weight suddenly became unbalanced, and it immediately capsized when the second wave struck. Only eight people on board survived. Fortunately, seeing the bad weather, half of the 600 excursionists stayed on the island, avoiding the shared fate. However, the number of deaths is between 250 and 300, many of whom are women and children. Tonight, thousands of relatives of the deceased are mourning at the piers in Nantes and here, a scene of utter desolation.

Paris, 15th (National News Agency) – It is now believed that 442 people perished in the waves after the Saint-Philibert ship accident. According to the latest information, there were 461 tourists in total, with only eight rescued. Another 17 people avoided disaster because they suffered from seasickness and stayed on the island. So far, four female corpses have been recovered.

Arctic Exploration Submarine Unable to Withstand Wind and Waves

Machinery Experiences Problems

U.S. Warships Rush to Rescue

New York, 14th (Reuters) – The large submarine Nautilus, which departed from Groton, Massachusetts, on June 5th, bound for London, experienced machinery damage in the Atlantic Ocean and could not proceed. The U.S. merchant ship Independence Hall is monitoring the situation, and the U.S. warships Arkansas and Wyoming are also rushing to assist. Once the waves calm down, they plan to tow the submarine to the nearest port. The famous Arctic explorer Sir Hubert Wilkins is currently on board the submarine. He plans to use this submarine to navigate underwater from Spitsbergen directly to the North Pole. When the submarine left Groton, it carried enough food for a year and a half and enough fuel for 4,000 to 5,000 miles of navigation. According to a report from the U.S. ship President Roosevelt, the Nautilus submarine's starboard motor is damaged, but the port motor is intact, so it can still move under its own power.

Greece Owes Old Debt to Russia

Soviet Russia Demands Repayment of Principal and Interest

Athens, 14th (National News Agency) – It is reported that Soviet Russia is now demanding that the Greek government repay the principal and interest on loans made to Greece by the Russian Imperial government, totaling 300 million gold francs. However, Greece is demanding that Soviet Russia compensate for or return the property of overseas Greeks confiscated after the revolution.

Eurasian Transportation Conference

Opened Yesterday in Tokyo

A List of Main Proposals

Tokyo, 15th (Denstu) – The 6th Eurasian International Passenger Transport Conference opened at 9:30 this morning in the Prime Minister's official residence. Attendees from foreign countries included representatives from Russian State Railways, German State Railways, German Northern Railway Company, Polish State Railways, Lithuanian State Railways, North German Lloyd, Canadian Pacific Railway, Chinese Eastern Railway, Italian State Railways, Da Lai Steamship Company, and Sovtorgflot. From the Japanese side, there were 35 representatives from Japanese National Railways, Korean Railways, South Manchuria Railway, Japanese Steamship Company, Osaka Shosen Kaisha, and North Japan Steamship Company. In addition, there were several foreign observers. This is the first large-scale conference held by Japanese National Railways. Following a welcoming address by Railway Minister Eguchi, Ms. Sfenli from Russia was elected as chair. The meeting decided (1) to establish a customs committee and (1) to establish a committee to attract foreign tourists, among other things. The meeting will continue until the 29th of this month. Starting July 1st, another committee and representatives will hold a Eurasian freight transport conference.

The central issue of this conference is the long-standing issue of Eurasian small-parcel joint transportation, which had preliminary solutions at the previous conference, as well as the establishment of a system for collecting payment for goods to facilitate trade, and the setting of round-the-world and Eastern Hemisphere travel tickets. In total, there are 35 items, the main ones being as follows: (1) Setting up a joint transportation plan for passengers and small parcels via Siberia and Switzerland, (1) Setting up a joint transportation plan for passengers and small parcels via Siberia, Canada, and around the world, (2) Handling the delivery and receipt of small parcels to and from various Pacific islands from Japanese ports, (1) Attracting American and Japanese tourists to travel via Siberia (presented by the above-mentioned administrators), (1) Setting up discounted round-trip tickets (presented by South Manchuria Railway), (1) Matters concerning Far East communication, (1) Opening through trains or through carriages in the following sections: (A) Changchun – Stolpce, (B) Changchun – Riga, (C) Vladivostok – Harbin – Stolpce, (D) Vladivostok – Harbin – Riga, (1) Matters concerning the fares for express trains on the Chinese Eastern Railway (presented by Japanese Railway Ministry), (1) Promoting the implementation of joint transportation of small parcels (presented by Japanese Railway Ministry), (1) The Eurasian joint transport group should take the same ratio for freight discount rates for each transportation agency (presented by Chinese Eastern Railway).

Soviet Russia's Economic Plan for China

Planning to Establish Large-Scale Sino-Russian Bank

Operating Import and Export and Banking Business

Harbin Correspondence – In recent years, Soviet Russia's policy toward China has been determined to carry out large-scale economic aggression. Last year, with Borli as its base, it organized an Economic Committee to develop trade with China, dumping the successful products of its Five-Year Economic Plan, which achieved significant results. This year, with the implementation of the state-run collectivized agriculture policy, the economic foundation has become even more solid. Its overall economic plan for China has been scheduled to be discussed at a meeting to be convened in Moscow on June 15th. All consuls-general stationed in Liaoning, such as Znamenski, and consuls-general stationed in Heilongjiang, such as Bobov, have returned home to participate in the meeting. Kuznetsky, the acting deputy director of the Chinese Eastern Railway, is also scheduled to return home within days to attend the meeting. It is faintly heard that the main agenda items of the meeting are about a dozen, roughly divided into economic development plans along the Chinese Eastern Railway, economic development plans in South Manchuria, and economic development plans along the Heilongjiang and Songhua River. After the meeting decides on each plan, it will order the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Russian consulates in the Eastern Provinces to jointly implement them step by step. However, before the implementation of this plan, Russia intends to first establish a bank in Northeast China, which will be larger in scale than the current Far Eastern Bank. The Far Eastern Bank's fund is 5 million rubles. The bank originally established branches in Shanghai, Guangzhou, Manzhouli, Liaoning, Tianjin, and Beiping, but since 1929, they were successively closed due to political or diplomatic reasons. Although various branches have tried their best to recover in recent years, they have either been disallowed by our authorities or, even if recovered, not trusted by the general public. Therefore, currently only the head office in Harbin is operating. Moreover, its reliance is only on the Chinese Eastern Railway's treasury. This year, the Chinese Eastern Railway's business is declining, and the bank is also affected. Therefore, at present, the bank is insufficient to be of use, whether due to political relations or financial strength. The Russian government is well aware of this situation, and therefore, at the beginning of the realization of its entire economic aggression plan against China, it intends to first establish a Sino-Russian bank as a treasury. In addition to having several times the capital of the Far Eastern Bank, its business purpose is to provide general banking services for deposits and loans, and also to engage in import and export business. Its nature is almost similar to Citibank in the United States, Korean Bank in Japan, Banque de l'Indochine in France, and HSBC in England. Although its starting point is the same as that of the Far Eastern Bank, its purpose is different. As for where the head office will be located, it will most likely be in Harbin or Liaoning. The branches will probably be in major ports in the Northeast and in Pingjin and Shanghai and Wuhan. The person in charge of this heavy responsibility is the newly appointed Russian Ambassador to Japan, Melinikov. Melinikov is the current Russian Consul in Harbin. He returned to Russia last month and has just returned. He was ordered by his government to investigate everything in detail and plans to go to Japan only after the investigation is completed. It is rumored that after the establishment of this bank, it will inherit the Chinese Eastern Railway's rights and interests of Daosheng Bank. The Chinese government should pay close attention to the truth of this statement (10th).

The Issue of Revising Loan Contracts in Sino-Japanese Railway Negotiations

Gao Jiyi Plans to Resign from the Key Negotiating Post

Extreme Disputes in Various Railway Loan Contracts

Shenyang Correspondence – Since the Japanese government specially appointed Kimura, who has diplomatic experience, as the director of the negotiation section of the South Manchuria Railway Co., Ltd. to resolve the outstanding issues of railways in the Northeast, Kimura has come to Shenyang several times. At first, he engaged in ordinary socializing to connect with various parties' feelings. Then, he put forward a proposal, saying that the two sides would only conduct ordinary talks and not in a formal negotiating manner. Finally, he personally went to inspect the lines of various loan-supplying railways to prepare for a response. His step-by-step approach was intended to establish himself in an absolutely advantageous position. However, looking at our side, the so-called specialized committee is only presided over by Yin Shousong. Although the other railway bureau directors nominally come to Shenyang once a week to perform their duties as specialized committee members, they are mostly exhausted by meaningless socializing and have long abandoned the negotiations. Gao Jiyi, the chairman of the Northeast Communications Committee, who is in charge of the most important matters, is running between Beijing and Peiping with Zhang Xueliang and has no time for this. Recently, there has even been talk of him feigning illness to avoid his post, and that Guo Jirun, the director of the Jichang Railway Bureau, will act on his behalf. Gao is usually very alert and knows that there will be no good outcome to this negotiation, so he is preparing to shirk responsibility. Guo, on the other hand, pursues empty fame and lacks practical ability, so it is feared that it will be difficult to achieve good results. Judging from the pre-negotiation situation of both parties, this negotiation is really not optimistic.

The Japanese side has put forward negotiating conditions, which include: 1. the issue of parallel lines, 2. the issue of freight competition, 3. the issue of revising loan contracts, and 4. the issue of completing the Jihui Line. In light of legal principles and facts, the first, second, and fourth items are not too difficult to deal with, as long as they are handled properly. The most difficult one, and all of which are factual issues, is the third item: the issue of revising loan contracts. The situation is described as follows: (1) The Sipingtaonan Railway: The railway's loan reached more than 50 million yuan, which is so large because no formal contract was signed, and it was only in the form of short-term loans. The annual interest rate was 9%. Every year, it was unable to pay the interest, so the contract was revised once, adding the interest to the principal and charging interest together. In addition, the government charged withdrawal management fees and rebates, so the actual amount used by the railway itself was only more than 20 million yuan. Of the remaining more than 30 million yuan, two-thirds were interest and one-third were management rebates and government withdrawals. Last year, when Zhou Peibing was the director, he discussed reducing the interest with the South Manchuria Railway. The South Manchuria Railway agreed to reduce it to 5%, but put forward the conditions: 1. a formal contract must be revised, 2. before the revision, the reduced interest would not be formal, but would be deducted from the joint transportation fee, 3. it would be responsible for introducing joint transportation between the South Manchuria Railway and other railways. After Zhou's consideration, although these were exchange conditions, they were all beneficial to our side and considered them acceptable. He immediately reported to the Northeast Communications Committee for a decision. However, the Communications Committee believed that reducing the interest was one thing, and revising the contract and joint transportation were another, and the two should not be confused. Moreover, since the South Manchuria Railway sincerely reduced the interest, it should not raise exchange conditions again. The joint transportation should also be initiated by our side and should not be proposed by the Japanese side. The bureau director was ordered to negotiate with the Japanese side according to this intention. Zhou was very angry, believing that the Japanese side had made this concession entirely due to his painstaking negotiations, but the meeting did not understand this. Feeling disheartened, he stopped talking about reducing the interest. Soon, Zhou resigned, and the case was shelved. Last year, the Communications Committee ordered each railway to submit opinions on revising the loan contracts in order to reorganize the various railway foreign debts. The railway stated the reduction of interest and the revision of the formal contract. This railway has fewer disputes among the railways borrowing in the Northeast, and the negotiation does not seem very difficult. (2) The Jidun Railway: This railway was contracted and built with funds advanced by the South Manchuria Railway. At first, it was 18 million yuan, but it was increased by 6 million yuan to 24 million yuan to repay Zhang Zuolin and improve the project. When it was completed last year, Zhao Zhen was the director, and he organized a completion evaluation committee, with the heads of the bureau's engineering and material departments and the Japanese chief engineer as members of the committee. He also appointed Zhong Jikong, the chief of the inspection section, as the chairman of the committee to preside over the matter. Zhong was a person with no common sense. After inspecting the line for a week, he sent a letter to the South Manchuria Railway in the name of the chairman of the completion evaluation committee to complete the work. Zhao resigned, and Li Duanpi took over as the director. At that time, it happened that the former director Wei Wuying was being investigated for various embezzlements and poor engineering, so he applied to the Communications Committee to hire engineering personnel from various railways to form another completion committee, and did not recognize the previous letter from Zhong Jikong, the completion evaluation committee, as valid. The committee was organized for several months and surveyed the line several times, preparing a report of thousands of words, pointing out three places where the project should be repaired extensively, more than seventy places where it should be repaired slightly, and more than one hundred and thirty places that did not conform to the original plan, and said that the highest price of the entire project was only more than 13 million yuan, and the remaining more than 10 million yuan was actually inflated, which our side could not recognize. Please verify. The committee sent the original to the railway bureau and ordered it to negotiate with the South Manchuria Railway quickly. However, the South Manchuria Railway refused to recognize it and handed over Zhong Jikong's original letter of completion, considering it as proof that our side had already completed the work. According to the contract, the South Manchuria Railway should accrue interest from the date of completion. Our side refused to accrue interest on the grounds that the work had not yet been completed, while the South Manchuria Railway calculated interest from the date of receiving Zhong's letter. Both sides had their own reasons and refused to give in to each other. The most difficult thing is how to deal with Zhong's letter. Zhong had already resigned with Zhao Zhen. It is now heard that there is a proposal to arrest him. It is not known whether it can be done or not. (3) The Taonai Railway: This railway is of the same nature as the Jidun Railway. The advance payment is still small, but there are other disputes. However, there is an item of expenses that the South Manchuria Railway has listed as high as more than 2 million yuan. After repeated negotiations by the railway bureau, it initially agreed to reduce it by tens of thousands of yuan, but then refused to concede any further. The railway had no choice but to submit it to the Communications Committee to request the committee to negotiate. However, the committee still ordered the bureau to handle it. The South Manchuria Railway will never concede this matter. The bureau has negotiated more than a dozen times, but it is still difficult to comply. The most fatal injury to this railway is the loan contract for residual materials and coal prices. Coal is the most important thing used by the railway. The railway has always purchased it from the South Manchuria Railway, and the price is very high. When the payment is due, a short-term loan contract is signed, with an annual interest rate of 9%. If the interest cannot be repaid on time, the interest is added to the principal and interest is charged together. The South Manchuria Railway sells coal to the railway at a price that is as high as more than 20 Japanese yen per ton. If the compound interest is multiplied, the price of each ton of coal will be about 100 yuan according to the current gold price. Someone said that coal alone is enough to ruin the Taonan Railway. According to a person from the Communications Committee, the committee could not cope with the railway's request to approve the inclusion of interest into the original principal each time, because if it approved the request, the loss would be too great and the matter too important. If the request was not approved, the railway would not be able to pay. It is now heard that it is planned to purchase more domestic coal to save it a little. (4) The Jichang Railway: The terms of the loan contract for this railway are the harshest among the loan contracts for state-owned railways. The South Manchuria Railway sends a representative to the bureau to direct the operation and business affairs, and his power is several times higher than that of the director. Previously, when Quan Liang and Wei Wuying were the directors, they were still able to rely on their qualifications or precision to manage things in many ways, and they still knew how to negotiate and handle things when things happened. Now, the South Manchuria Railway representative acts arbitrarily. If he is questioned even slightly, he uses the loan contract as a talisman, often citing the different interpretations of the text of the contract, resulting in repeated disputes that cannot be resolved. The loan contract for Jidun stipulates that when the formal contract is revised upon completion, it may be merged with Jichang. On the Japanese side, it is planned to use the original Jichang contract as the blueprint, while our side had previously planned to follow the Tianjin-Pukou contract. Now that things have changed, a separate plan will of course be proposed. However, since the Japanese side has obtained rights, it will never easily give in. This is another factual difficulty. (June 9th)

Freight Train Derailed on the Canton-Hankow Railway

Over Twenty Lengths of Track Destroyed, Two Trains Overturned

One Laborer Injured, Over Ten Pigs and Cattle Killed

The railway tracks along the Guangzhou to Shaozhou section of the Canton-Hankow Railway have been in disrepair for some time, resulting in frequent train derailments. On the 6th of this month, at 6:00 AM, the 22nd freight train from Shaozhou to Guangzhou, consisting of five cars, experienced such an incident. The first two cars were carrying livestock such as pigs and cattle, the third and fourth carried firewood, and the fifth carried rice and stone. After unloading goods along the way, the train reached Xiaoping Station at 3:10 PM. At this point, the railway track suddenly gave way under the excessive weight, and over twenty lengths of track, including the rail and sleepers at the 280th marker, were destroyed. The driver was unable to brake in time, and as a result, the first two cars derailed and overturned into the fields. Fortunately, the third and fourth cars stopped quickly, averting a more serious accident. Personnel from that railway section hurriedly reported to the Guangshao Railway Bureau, stating that the 21st freight train had derailed between the 282nd and 282nd marker, and only came to a stop at the 273rd marker (i.e., Tangxikou). Two covered cars were found overturned on the roadside, and the remaining three covered cars and one guard car had also derailed, but had not overturned. There were no other issues. The cars were towed back to Huangsha. Twenty-five steel rails were found detached from the sleepers, and the bolts of the fishplates were broken. Upon receiving the report, the Railway Bureau immediately dispatched over a hundred workers with steel rails and sleepers to carry out repairs. Upon arrival, they used cranes to hoist the overturned cars one by one. The repairs to the railway track were completed by the morning of the 7th. In this accident, only one laborer in the first two cars was slightly injured. In addition, two or three oxen and eight or nine pigs were killed. Over twenty lengths of track were damaged. Therefore, the passenger train that departed from Yingde at 7:15 AM on the 7th was unable to pass through when it arrived at Xiaoping at 3:00 PM in the afternoon. Passengers had to disembark and walk across the damaged track at Dalang Station before boarding a connecting train at Xicun to return to the provincial capital. On the afternoon of the 7th, over six hundred passengers heading to the North River arrived at the Huangsha Main Station to wait for the train north. However, they waited until 2:30 PM, but no southbound passenger train arrived. Later, a telephone report from Xiaoping stated that the passenger train would not be able to reach the provincial capital that afternoon. The passengers at the station were disappointed and returned. According to the Railway Bureau, the damaged track was not fully repaired until 3:00 or 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 7th. Therefore, all trains were able to resume normal service between Shaozhou and Guangzhou on the morning of the 8th. (June 8th)

Itinerary of the Sino-French Expedition

Passed Suiyuan Wuni Usu

After departing from Beiping, the Sino-French Expedition reached Wuni Usu in Suiyuan on May 26th, after leaving Bailingmiao on May 24th. The distance between these places is 269 kilometers, approximately 1,000 kilometers from Beiping. Along the way, many yellow sheep were seen. The team hunted three, sufficient to provide meat for a week. The journey passed through areas devoid of trees, and even the grass was not very lush due to the late season. In the three days of travel, only a few Mongolian families and about a dozen Han Chinese merchants doing business in the Mongolian grasslands were seen, all enduring extreme hardship. The only means of transportation was camel caravans, traveling at most forty or fifty li per day, with mules and camels needing regular rest and grazing. There were many quicksands, sinking to ankle depth, and numerous small stones. The daily climate variations were quite large, embodying the saying "wear fur coats in the morning and gauze in the afternoon." Local security, maintained by Mongolian guerrilla forces, was relatively peaceful. On May 27th, the expedition proceeded to Sande Temple, approximately one hundred kilometers away, a journey that could be completed in a day. When the vehicles stopped, those responsible for collecting plants and animals and conducting geological surveys were extremely busy.

Jiangsu Province's Spring Silkworm Egg Production Industry This Year

Estimated Production of 2,294,000 Sheets

In recent years, Jiangsu Province has seen rapid progress in both public and private efforts to improve the silkworm egg industry. According to surveys, there are now over 140 improved egg production farms. In previous years, improved eggs were rare, and most farmers relied on local Yu Hang breeds. One dan of dried cocoons required over three dan of fresh cocoons to produce when using local breeds, while improved cocoons required only two dan of fresh cocoons to produce one dan of dried cocoons. Therefore, improved cocoons are worth ten to twenty yuan more per dan than local cocoons. In the event of adverse weather, local breeds are almost completely wiped out, while improved breeds are more resistant to the weather and less likely to fail. Farmers in rural areas, especially in northern Jiangsu, were initially skeptical of improved breeds. After years of comparison, they have all come to trust caged breeds (local people call improved breeds "caged breeds"). One catty of local cocoons used to yield only one tael of silk, while improved cocoons can yield one tael and eight mace of silk. In the future, local breeds will inevitably lose their market. However, our country's only major rival is Japan. Every year, in addition to competing with our country in the European and American markets with their increasingly refined silk, Japan also imports large quantities of inferior breeds into our country. According to investigations, the first batch of spring eggs imported this year amounted to 300,000 sheets. Jiangsu Province's annual sales volume is only about ten million. If no measures are taken to resist this, not only will our country's egg production industry have no business guarantee, but it is also hateful that they import inferior silkworm eggs into our country, preventing thorough improvement in our country. According to statistics from the Provincial Silkworm Industry Supervision Office, the total amount of spring and autumn silkworm eggs produced by public and private egg production farms in Jiangsu this spring is approximately 2,294.4 taels. At 1,000 sheets of silkworm eggs per tael, this means that over 2,294,000 sheets of silkworm eggs can be produced. Even if Japanese eggs are completely blocked, demand will still outstrip supply.

Suzhou

Robbery by Bandits in Shenjiazhai and Shashang Village: Shenjiazhai and Shashang Village, under the jurisdiction of the urban district outside Fengmen Gate, are located approximately twelve miles from the city. They consist of over one hundred households, whose residents are primarily engaged in agriculture and are generally quite prosperous. On the morning of the 14th, around 2:00 AM, four bandit boats suddenly arrived from the direction of Dushu Lake, entering Donggang and reaching Shenjiazhai. The boats carried over thirty bandits, dressed in various dark grey short jackets and wearing black casual hats. They were armed with flashlights, quick-firing guns, and box cannons, dividing into two groups. From two of the bandit boats, more than ten bandits landed in Shenjiazhai and first broke down the door of Shen Zhengxiang's house at number thirty-seven, looting it. They then proceeded to ransack house after house: Xu Shuigen, Xu Hongxiang, Xu Yuanxiang, Shen Fei's, Shen Hongxiang, Gu Xiangfu, Shen Suixing, Shen Faming, Shen Huiquan, and Qiu Shengfu. Simultaneously, the other two bandit boats sailed across the river and through the Shashang Bridge eastward to Shashang Village, robbing Xu Dexiang, Gu Genjin, Xu Caigao, Zhu Jinmao, Gu Xufa, Gu Zhixiang, Zhang Shengfa, Zhang Shengfu, Zhang Shengrong, Zhu Yeguang, Gu Yuxiang, Zhu Xiangfa, Gu Qixiang, Zhu Wan's, He Xiaogou, and Zhou Zhaoquan, totaling sixteen households. Afterwards, the group that robbed Shenjiazhai took their loot onto their boats and sailed along the river to Shashang Village to meet with the two bandit boats that had robbed Shashang Village. They fired shots into the air as a warning and proceeded eastward towards Huangshi Bridge in Lü'anqiao, turning south towards Huangtiandang and passing through Jinji Lake towards Chefang. Before leaving, they announced that they would rob Chefang again. The losses in both villages were estimated at over three thousand yuan.

Kunshan

Superintendent Dismissed and Investigated: Qin Jieren, Director of the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau, learned the other day that Superintendent Wu Songying was inspecting travelers at the Dadong Hotel. In room thirteen, he found a local man, Ni Songlin, cohabiting with a tailor's wife, Qian. Deeming their behavior inappropriate, Wu Songying took them to the bureau for questioning but privately released them mid-journey after receiving a bribe of twenty yuan. Director Qin dispatched Inspector Zhang Tian to investigate, and the report was confirmed. On the 15th, the superintendent was first dismissed and then sent to the county for further investigation.

Detective Team Captures Kidnappers: Wu Yunzhou, a resident of Xiema Bridge and Heshangbang, along with two of his nieces (from Zhangpu), were kidnapped by bandits last month. The other day, Wu Shaokang, captain of the county's detective team, apprehended a bandit named Zhou Heshang in Shanghai. Zhou confessed to following the bandit leader Zhou Er Mazi to commit the kidnapping. Currently, Zhou and the hostages are at Yidaizijiao in Shanghai. According to Zhou's confession, Captain Wu reported to County Magistrate Pang, requesting a warrant to lead detectives to Shanghai. They cooperated with the local police station and captured the bandit leader Zhou Er Mazi and bandits Lü A'er and five others inside the Qunle Teahouse in Yidaizijiao. The hostages were not found during the search. The Wang bandits were escorted to Kunshan on the 14th and handed over to the County Public Security Bureau. After interrogation by Director Qin, the bandits confessed to the kidnapping of the Wu family. They stated that the hostages were hidden in a boat in the river near Yidaizijiao. Director Qin detained the bandits temporarily and ordered Captain Wu to go to Shanghai to search for the hostages. On the morning of the 15th, the County Public Security Bureau received a telegram from Captain Wu in Shanghai stating that the hostages had been found and would be escorted back to Kunshan soon.

Wuxi

Silk Factories Request Exemption from Business Tax: Regarding the issue of levying business tax on silk factories in Wuxi, the industry association previously sent a letter to the County Chamber of Commerce, requesting it to forward a letter to the Business Tax Bureau, stating that it would be difficult to bear the business tax before the export tax was abolished. The bureau submitted a report to the provincial authorities for review. An order was then received stating, "The business tax is levied based on capital and turnover, which is different from taxes levied on goods. Silk factories fall within the scope of manufacturing and should be subject to business tax. The export tax is a customs revenue, unrelated to the abolition of 'li' taxes, and even less related to business tax. The request should not be discussed." Upon receiving the order, the industry referred to Article 1 of the National Regulations and Article 2 of the Jiangsu Province Business Tax Regulations, which state that all special taxes already levied by the central government and those with separate central regulations are exempt from business tax. Furthermore, the new export tariff schedule has been officially announced by the National Government, with item 181 of the fourth category listing white silk and silk reeling factories, with a tax of fifteen taels of silver per dan. Therefore, this export tax is clearly regulated by the central government and is consistent with the exception stipulated in Article 2 of the Jiangsu Province Business Tax Regulations. Moreover, the export tax is indeed a central government revenue, which also aligns with the provision in Article 1 of the Business Tax Outline that excludes special taxes levied by the central government. If it is said that silk factories fall within the scope of manufacturing and should be subject to business tax, then why are yarn factories, which also fall within the scope of manufacturing, able to be excluded? If it is said that yarn and flour factories are exempt from business tax because the central government levies a consolidated tax on them, then the silk export tax is also levied by the central government, which is the same principle. Why discriminate against silk factories alone? Moreover, silk factories are engaged in foreign trade, and the government should provide special protection to them. However, levying both export tax and business tax seems contrary to the government's intention to protect international trade. Yesterday, the industry again sent the above information to the County Chamber of Commerce, requesting it to forward it to the Business Tax Bureau and to submit it to the central and provincial authorities, requesting approval for exemption from business tax in order to comply with the central government's intentions.

Revision of Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Matters: In order to consolidate tax revenue, the Ministry of Finance recently abolished the previous contractor system and uniformly changed it to direct commissioning. The previous tobacco and alcohol transit tax, which resembled "li" tax, was decided to be abolished. The tax rates for public sales licenses were increased to compensate. Currently, the Jiangsu Province Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau is dividing the entire province into tax districts. The tax rates for public sales and license sales are divided into thirty-two districts, and the license tax is divided into ten districts. The tax rates for public sales and licenses are each increased by 30%. The total amount for the entire province is estimated to be over 1.9 million yuan. The list of candidates for the heads of the district branches has also been submitted by Bureau Chief Guan Yinlun to the Ministry of Finance for approval. Gu Daosheng from Wuxi has been appointed as the Chief of the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Branch in Chuan Chongqi, with an annual quota of slightly less than 90,000. Chen Henian has been appointed as the Chief of the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Branch in Wu Kunjiang Chang Taijia, with an annual quota of slightly over 100,000 yuan. Yu Yunqing is the Chief of the Wuxi Tobacco and Alcohol Public Sales Branch. The Wuxi Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax is under the jurisdiction of the Wuxi Yin District, and the position of Chief of the Collection Branch has been appointed to Yun Fubin from Changzhou. Chen Henian, who was originally the Chief of the Wuxi Stamp Tax Bureau, has been replaced by Mao Xieding. The handover is expected to take place soon.

Wujin Business Tax Bureau Detains Dry Cocoon Boats: After fifteen silk factories, including Yongtai Gan and Shen, opposed the business tax on the cocoon industry, a resolution has yet to be reached. The Wujin Business Tax Bureau, due to the lack of a confirmed method for taxing the cocoon industry in the county, has dispatched personnel to various cocoon businesses to collect taxes separately. However, the cocoon season this year has been poor and has already ended for those who started early. A checkpoint has been established in Henglin Town, requiring all dry cocoons being transported to complete the business tax payment. Whenever cocoon boats pass by, they are ordered to stop for inspection. Most of the silk factories in Wuxi purchase cocoons from Yixing, Piaoyang, Jintan, Danyang, and other counties. They must pass through Henglin when transporting the cocoons back, and they are all intercepted and ordered to pay the business tax. Yesterday, dry cocoons transported from Jintan by Yongtai Silk Factory were also detained and have not been released yet. Upon hearing this, the silk factories believe that silk merchants are being disturbed by disguised checkpoints after the abolition of "li" taxes, which violates the central government's intention not to burden the people or hinder commercial development. They have decided to report the illegal actions of the head of the county's Business Tax Bureau to the central government and the Control Yuan for rectification. Railway Police Department Investigates Allegations: Yang Chunxiang (from Anhui Taozhou), owner of the Yuelai Teahouse on Hanchang Road outside Guangfu Gate, carried meeting funds to Dadesheng Grocery Store in Zhoushanbang to participate in a rotating credit association at 2:00 PM on the 4th of this month. While passing by the station, he was stopped by railway patrol officer Zhang Baokun, who fabricated accusations to Section Chief Feng of the Wuxi Station Police Section. Section Chief Feng, without careful inquiry, arrested Yang, locked him with iron chains, and extorted a confession through torture. After Yang argued reasonably, Section Chief Feng reluctantly transferred him to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Upon learning of this, the Anhui Native Association in Wuxi felt greatly aggrieved and sent an official letter to the Public Security Bureau, requesting justice and a thorough investigation of the false accusation. After being bailed out by the association, Yang hired lawyer Tang Ying to file a lawsuit with the County Court. Meanwhile, he reported to the Anhui Native Association in Wuxi, requesting justice. The association submitted separate reports to the Ministry of Railways, the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, and the Police Department, requesting a thorough investigation and severe punishment. After receiving the report, the Police Department dispatched someone named Yang to Wuxi yesterday to investigate. After confirming the facts, they returned to Shanghai to report.

Tao Tingfang Intimidates and Extorts Money: Sun Zuhong, a lawyer from this county, was previously resented by Tao Tingfang and Tao Zhusun because he refused their commission. The Tao family falsely accused lawyer Sun on the pretext. On the 6th of this month, while lawyer Sun Zuhong was having lunch at the Recuperation Hospital inside Guangfu Gate, Tao Tingfang used intimidation to extort 200 silver dollars from lawyer Sun, with the assistance of Tao's friend, Yang Yunqiu, in the extortion. Lawyer Sun Zuhong immediately filed a complaint with the County Court's Prosecutor's Office, stating the facts. After receiving the complaint, the Prosecutor's Office issued an order yesterday to summon them for a hearing on a scheduled date.

Changzhou

Police Team Captures Multiple Bandits: Yu Shiquan, captain of the First Platoon of the Pan Shu Town Police in Wuyi County, dispatched his team on the morning of the 14th, around 1:00 AM, to join the Jiangyin Xiqiao Town Defense Corps in suppressing bandits in the Huagang Kou area. They captured four suspects, Yan Shenglin, Wang Dehai, Lü Heshang, and Zhang Bing Yatou, inside the Wudou Temple. Advancing to the Jia Hui Village area, they captured Jiang Genfu and found a Type 2 wooden-cased gun, eight bullets, and military uniforms in the water tank of his house. Subsequently, they apprehended Xie Zhaohai, who was acting suspiciously. All were sent to the platoon headquarters for preliminary interrogation. Jiang Genfu confessed to committing robbery, while the other suspects were evasive. Captain Yu dispatched his team on the 15th to escort them to the city and hand them over to the county for further investigation.

Three Sailing Boats Robbed En Route: Three sailing boats from Lijiabridge, Maojiabridge, and Nanzhai in Wuyi County were robbed at gunpoint while passing through the Nanni Bridge area in the Sixth District around 1:00 AM on the 14th. The total losses for the three boats amounted to several hundred yuan. Afterwards, the Sixth District Office reported to the county government, requesting an investigation.

Ancient Artifacts from the Ming Dynasty Discovered in a Desolate Tomb: Zhang and Li, two farmers from Zhenwumiao in Yangzhou County, discovered an ancient copper coin and a green glazed censer in a desolate tomb in Tangzitou. The censer had the inscription "Chongzhen Eighth Year," indicating that it was an artifact from the Ming Dynasty. It is reported that Zhang and Li intend to take these artifacts to Yangzhou for sale.

Third Sheet

Educational News Highlights

Ministry of Education's Interpretation Regarding Academic System and Educational Association Members

The Ministry of Education received a telegram from the Shaanxi Education Department stating that in order to seek education for students and Shaanxi's need for talent, it is proposed to recruit a number of senior high school graduates and provide funding for them to study at designated domestic universities. However, Shaanxi Province has not had senior high schools before. The high school reorganized from Xi'an Zhongda University has not yet reached the graduation period. At a time when talent is lacking, cultivation cannot be delayed. It is now proposed to strictly examine graduates from the old-system middle schools according to the senior high school level, approve a quota, and provide funding to various schools for further studies. Considering the situation in the disaster-stricken Northwest, can it be considered and accommodated? Respectfully request instructions to follow. The Ministry of Education replied, "Graduates from the old-system middle school are equivalent to the first grade of the current senior high school system and cannot directly enter the university. However, the admission qualifications for specialized schools have a provision for admitting one-fifth of those with equivalent academic ability to senior high school graduation. Please refer to it." The Ministry of Education also received a telegram from the Hebei Education Department stating that it had approved a letter from the Hebei Provincial Party Affairs Reorganization Committee stating, "An investigation of the members of the education associations in various counties revealed that some library and newspaper reading room staff, education bureau document processing personnel, and lecturers do not seem to be considered educational administrative personnel and school staff." How should this be handled? As the case concerns the interpretation of laws and regulations, it is appropriate to telegram for verification. The Ministry of Education replied, "Libraries and newspaper reading rooms are social education institutions. Their staff, except for accountants, general affairs staff, clerks, and secretaries, in accordance with Article 16, paragraph 1 of the Education Association Law, may not be members of the education association. Other staff members have the qualifications of members of the education association. As for the staff of the Education Bureau, all staff members above the rank of section member and equivalent to section members are current educational administrative personnel. In accordance with Article 16, paragraph 2 of the Education Association Law, they may be members of the education association. You are hereby notified."

Ministry of Education Explains Three Difficult Points of the Junior High School Credit System

The Ministry of Education received a request from Jinan University for an explanation of three difficult points of the credit system in the junior high school department. The Ministry of Education instructed, "We have received your request. The difficult points you mentioned regarding the implementation of the credit system are answered separately as follows: (1) The awarding of credits should be based on academic performance. Students who study a required course for one academic year and fail in the first semester should, in principle, retake it in the second semester. However, this often causes difficulties in schools that only have autumn semester start classes. The remedy should be determined based on the number of students who failed. If the number of students is large, in addition to continuing to study the second semester of the course, the school should also open a special class at the same time to supplement the first semester's coursework. If the number of students is small and not enough to open a special class, they should be allowed to continue studying the second semester of the course while supplementing the first semester's coursework on their own outside of class or during holidays. Only after passing the make-up exam can the credit for the first semester be granted. It is said that some students in the school have failed in the first semester but passed in the second semester. These students should choose a time to retake the first semester's coursework and should not be exempted from the exam and directly granted the credit for the first semester. (2) Promotion in the credit system should be determined based on whether the number of failed credits exceeds the limit set by each school. Those who have not exceeded the set limit should be allowed to be promoted. However, the number of credits they study after promotion should be restricted so that they have time to retake the courses they failed. The school should consider this when setting the timetable and try to avoid conflicts. If it is unavoidable, the two methods shown in the previous article should be used to remedy it. (3) If a student has reached the graduation period but still fails one required course, they should be allowed to make it up outside the school. They should be allowed to study outside the school until the end of the semester or academic year and then return to school for a make-up exam. It is not necessary to let them stay in school to retake the course. The formal graduation certificate should be issued after passing the make-up exam. You should follow the instructions above."

Shaanxi Education Department Emphasizes Examinations

Regulations for Semester and Graduation Examinations

The Education Department of Shaanxi Province has stipulated the dates for summer vacation for all schools in the province this year. To strictly evaluate student performance, the Education Department has further stipulated two methods for this year's examinations, which are detailed below:

A. Semester or Academic Year Examination Methods

1. The dates for semester or academic year examinations in each school should be determined by the school itself, based on the summer vacation dates stipulated by the Education Department, and a list should be submitted for approval.

2. Examinations should be held centrally as a principle.

3. For each course, the teacher should prepare twice the number of questions, and the principal should randomly select the questions. Additional questions, up to half the original number, may be added for testing purposes.

4. It is absolutely forbidden to reveal the scope of the exam, engage in bribery, or collude to deceive or conceal poor student performance.

5. The Education Department will send personnel to supervise the examinations at each school.

6. Supervisors have the right to change a portion or all of the test questions, but the scope must be limited to the materials the students have learned.

7. Supervisors have the right to change the examination location and procedures.

8. After the examinations, each school should calculate the scores according to past practice and submit a list for approval.

9. An examination hall regulation is attached, which must be strictly followed during the examinations.

B. Graduation Examination Methods

1. The Education Department will send personnel to supervise the graduation examinations at each school. When necessary, the supervisor may designate the examination location and assign faculty and staff to assist in the supervision.

2. The Education Department will create a register of the graduating students' academic records from previous years and report it to the department.

3. The textbooks or lecture notes used by the graduating students during this semester should be listed in detail, indicating the starting and ending paragraphs, in accordance with the Education Department's Order No. 1940. A complete set of teaching materials for each subject should also be submitted to the department.

4. The scope of the graduation examinations will be the materials the students have learned. The Education Department will set the questions, which will be announced by the supervisor on the spot.

5. The examination papers should be sealed, and each school should prepare them.

6. After the examinations, the supervisor will seal and stamp the examination papers on the spot and take them back to the department for review and grading. After the grading, the papers will be returned to each school for calculation. Those who pass will have their diplomas filled out by the school and submitted to the department for verification and issuance.

7. The examination dates should be determined by each school based on the summer vacation dates stipulated by the Education Department and submitted in a list for approval.

8. The method for calculating graduation grades will be handled according to past practice.

9. An examination hall regulation is attached, which must be strictly followed during the examinations.

Attachment: Examination Hall Regulations

1. Take your assigned seat according to the designated number and do not move.

2. There will be a ten-minute question period after the questions are distributed. No questions will be allowed after that.

3. Do not whisper, look around, or deliberately leave your seat.

4. Do not pass or receive any documents.

5. Do not carry any notes or papers.

6. After submitting the paper, do not linger in the room or loiter outside, causing disturbances.

7. Submit the paper within the allotted time.

8. Those who violate the above regulations will be subject to penalties, including deduction of points, demerits, suspension, or expulsion.

Request for Increased Funding for Anhui Social Education

(Anhui News) The budget for social education in Anhui Province for the 20th year of the Republic is more than 17,600 yuan higher than that of the 19th year. The Provincial Government has not yet approved it. The Education Department submitted a proposal to the Provincial Government's Standing Committee on the 12th, requesting that it be approved as is. The total is 85,920 yuan per year, an increase of 17,652 yuan over the 19th year.

Wuhan University Prepares to Establish Research Institutes

Starting in the 20th Year of the Republic

Article 7 of the Organizational Regulations of National Wuhan University originally stipulated the establishment of research institutes. The school believes that the campus buildings are nearing completion, and the basic equipment of the colleges of Liberal Arts, Science, Law, and Engineering is gradually being completed. Starting in the 20th year of the Republic, the colleges of Liberal Arts, Law, and Science will all have senior students. To facilitate further studies for graduates and to conduct systematic research on the practical problems of industry and commerce and other scientific problems in the Central China provinces, the 123rd school affairs meeting resolved to prepare for the establishment of research institutes in each college starting in the 20th year. The preparation period for each research institute is set at one year. During the preparation period, each research institute will establish research professorships and expand the equipment for research as much as possible. When half of the research institutes in each college are completed, the university-wide research institute will be officially established. It is reported that the school affairs meeting has also resolved that President Wang Shijie will begin planning the funding. Meanwhile, Deans Pi Zongshi of the Law College, Wang Xinggong of the Science College, Chen Yuan of the Liberal Arts College, and Shao Yizhou of the Engineering College will be responsible for reviewing the detailed measures. All plans for implementation will be finalized during the summer vacation.

Hanqing Education Fund Subsidy for Primary and Secondary School Teachers' Salaries

(Shenyang Correspondence) The Liao Hanqing Education Fund Board of Directors was established by Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang, who donated five million yuan of his private property to honor the last wishes of the Grand Marshal. The fund is used to subsidize the public primary and secondary education in Liaoning Province as a permanent fund. The board is composed of enthusiastic educators who are responsible for the custody and distribution of the fund. The entire amount is deposited in the official banks of the Three Northeastern Provinces at a monthly interest rate of 1.2%, yielding a monthly interest of 60,000 yuan and an annual interest of 720,000 yuan. In addition to subsidies, awards, and incentives, the measures for subsidizing the salaries of primary and secondary school teachers are sufficient to promote and encourage public attention to primary and secondary education. This kind of treatment is unprecedented in other provinces in the country, and it is enough to make many poor scholars envious. It is no coincidence that education in Liaoning has been thriving and making rapid progress in recent years. The standard for the distribution of the subsidy is based on the county unit. All primary and secondary school teachers in each county (including principals who do not also teach courses) are evaluated based on their years of service and the quality of their teaching performance and divided into four grades: A, B, C, and D. Each year, the board of directors entrusts the county education bureau to conduct investigations, evaluations, and reports based on the standards set by the board. After the board of directors approves the reports, the full amount of the subsidy to which the county's teachers are entitled is issued to the education bureau for distribution. Provincial schools are treated as a single unit, and the board of directors entrusts the education department to handle the matter in accordance with the previous procedures. No subsidy is given to primary and secondary school teachers with less than three years of service. Those who are evaluated as Grade A will receive an annual subsidy of 30 yuan, Grade B 26 yuan, Grade C 23 yuan, and Grade D none. Those who continue to serve in a school for more than five years will receive an additional 5 yuan, more than ten years an additional 10 yuan, more than fifteen years an additional 15 yuan, more than twenty years an additional 20 yuan, more than twenty-five years an additional 25 yuan, and more than thirty years an additional 30 yuan. Those who retire after twenty years of service will receive half of their final year's subsidy as a retirement pension for up to five years. Those who retire after twenty-five years of service will receive the pension for up to ten years. Those who retire after thirty years of service will receive the pension for life. If a teacher receiving a retirement pension dies, in addition to the current year's retirement pension, an additional two years' retirement pension will be issued as a survivor's benefit. Regarding the years of service, those who have completed three years or more as of the end of June of the 19th year of the Republic will be considered to have completed three years. The board of directors has completed the review of the subsidy for this year, which has been reported by each county, and it has been decided that it will be distributed separately in late this month.

Local News

Preliminary Entrance Examination for Graduates of Unregistered Private Senior High Schools

Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice regarding the preliminary entrance examination for graduates of unregistered private senior high schools in the city. The notice stated, "The preliminary entrance examination for graduates of unregistered private senior high schools in this city will be held again during the summer vacation this year. The regulations were previously drafted, submitted to the Ministry of Education for registration, and announced for implementation. It has now been decided that the examination will be held on July 1st. Registration will begin on June 16th and end on June 28th. Graduates of unregistered private senior high schools or equivalent schools in this city who aspire to further their education, as well as graduates of unregistered private senior high schools from any location who were admitted as auditors to the first year of public or registered private colleges or universities in this city in the 19th year of the Republic, should personally submit their graduation certificates, two recent 4.5-inch half-length photos, and a registration fee of one yuan to the Bureau during the registration period. Those auditing first-year university courses should also submit proof of auditing. Collect the regulations during registration and wait for the examination date. This is hereby announced."

Income and Expenditure of the 15th North China Games

Income of 123,500

Expenditure of 121,100

Jinan Correspondence, the 15th North China Games closed. The Organizing Committee is handling the closing matters. Yesterday, the committee released the list of income and expenditure of the conference. As of June 11, the total income was 123,578.60 yuan, and the total expenditure was 121,163.41 yuan. After offsetting the income and expenditure, the total balance was 2,415.19 yuan. The list of income and expenditure is disclosed below:

Income: (1) Donations, totaling 27,100 yuan; (2) Conference expenses, totaling 16,911 yuan (received from the Finance Department); (3) Construction expenses, totaling 77,275 yuan (received from the Finance Department); (4) Advertising fees, totaling 193 yuan; (5) Conference program booklet, totaling 99.60 yuan (sale price). The total income above is 123,578.60 yuan.

Expenditure: (1) Construction expenses, totaling 94,275 yuan (it was found that the construction expenses totaled 79,275 yuan received from the Finance Department, and 15,000 yuan was moved from donations); (2) Conference expenses, totaling 21,963.53 yuan (in addition to 16,911 yuan received from the Finance Department, 5,052.53 yuan was moved from donations); (3) Construction department staff subsidies for April and May, totaling 746 yuan (moved from donations); (4) Miscellaneous expenses of the construction department, totaling 248.12 yuan (moved from donations); (5) Expenses for the deputy chairmen to entertain guests and players from various provinces and cities, totaling 2,089.96 yuan; (6) Land price of the sports field, totaling 699.80 yuan (moved from donations); (7) Fees for buying land deeds, registering stamps, brokers, and advertisements, totaling 141 yuan (moved from donations). The total expenditure above is 121,163.41 yuan.

The remaining balance is 2,415.19 yuan.
