Special Issue No. 3 of the National Jinan University on the Occasion of the Fourth Anniversary of the Establishment of the University and the Twenty-Fifth Anniversary of the Founding of the School

A Review of Our School's Twenty-Fifth Anniversary

— Xu Minyi

Time flies like an arrow, and the days and months never linger. The world's affairs are ever-changing and unpredictable. Everything either progresses or regresses; there is no middle ground. Since its inception, our school has, in the blink of an eye, reached its twenty-fifth anniversary. Like a child, it has grown into a mature adult through arduous years. With burgeoning vitality, it is at the prime of its usefulness. Though it has experienced hardships and even faced a period of stagnation, those who have led the school since its recovery have been determined to manage it diligently and bring about innovative advancements. They have ultimately created this solemn and magnificent institution, the only overseas Chinese university in the country, standing tall in Zhenru, west of Shanghai. However, over these twenty-five years, I wonder how much heart's blood has been poured out and how many public funds of the nation have been expended. Tracing back to the thirty-third year of the Guangxu reign of the late Qing Dynasty, Liangjiang Governor-General Duan Fang memorialized and received approval to establish our school in Nanjing's Xuejia Alley, using the Miaoxiang Nunnery as its premises. The first director was none other than our current President Zheng. The following year, it was reorganized into a middle school. In the third year of the Xuantong reign, Director Zheng was transferred elsewhere, and Jiangning's Yang Xichang succeeded him. In March of that year, I returned to China from Panchanama in Borneo, Southeast Asia, bringing back two students, Hong Linfeng and Zheng Bowen. I sent them to the school and stayed there for three days, engaging in earnest conversations with Director Yang. I still remember his words: "Overseas Chinese youths are often of strong and straightforward character. If they are given proper education, the results will be significant. In the future, they can all become pillars of the nation." At that time, the school only had over twenty students sent back at the sole expense of Xu Boxing, the headman of the Chinese Council in Southeast Asia, and some students from Java, totaling no more than thirty. (Xu Boxing was the headman of the Chinese Council in Java and the president of the Chinese School. He returned to China to visit the Nanyang Industrial Exposition and died of illness in Shanghai.) In July of the autumn, I accepted an invitation from the Surabaya Chinese School in Java and returned to the tropics. After arriving in Surabaya, I also managed the affairs of the General Association of Dutch Schools, receiving letters from Director Yang informing me of school affairs and requesting me to promote the school. At that time, there was one most difficult matter to deal with, namely the twenty-odd students sent back by Xu Boxing. Because of Xu's death, no one was providing for their expenses, and the school had to lend them money. In less than a year, over five thousand taels had been advanced, greatly impacting the school's finances. Letters and telegrams were sent to the students' families to request repayment, but none ever repaid. When the Xinhai Revolution broke out, the school was immediately closed, and the students dispersed. Those with means returned to Southeast Asia on their own, while the rest lingered in Shanghai, lacking food and clothing and living in constant anxiety. They were then funded by the China and Foreign Life Insurance Company to return to Southeast Asia. This can be considered a small anecdote in the history of the school during the late Qing Dynasty. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, Yuan Xitao served as the Vice Minister of Education and appointed Huang Yanpei and others to restore Jinan School (later Huang and others became party affairs school trustees). In the spring of the seventh year, the ministry appointed Zhao Zhengping as the president, and the school reopened at its original site in Miaoxiang Nunnery. In the spring of the eighth year, I returned from Surabaya with ten students, including Wu Huaiqing, who were admitted to the school by President Zhao and entered the normal, commercial, and middle school departments (all of whom have since graduated and returned to Southeast Asia to work). At that time, the school already had three hundred students, and its scale was roughly established. In September, teacher Bai went to Southeast Asia, and President Zhao invited me to the school to teach and oversee documents. This was the beginning of my time at the school. In the summer of the ninth year, President Zhao resigned, and the ministry appointed Ke Chengyi to succeed him. He was particularly enthusiastic in planning school affairs and deeply trusted by the students. He specially sent teachers to the National Language Training Institute of the Ministry of Education in Beijing to attend lectures on the national language phonetic symbols. After graduating, they returned to the school to teach the normal students. In the autumn of the tenth year, President Ke resigned, and President Zhao returned to his post. He submitted a request to the authorities to issue 100,000 yuan of school bonds to purchase over 300 mu of land in Zhenru to build a new school building and organize Jinan New Village. It was completed in the autumn of the twelfth year, and the male students all moved there, while the female students remained at the Nanjing campus. I also came to Shanghai with them. In the thirteenth year, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War broke out, and the school building was occupied by troops. The entire school moved to Yichang Road in Shanghai, to the Dayou Oil Company. Although the war was fierce, education did not cease. In the autumn of the fourteenth year, President Zhao resigned, and Jiang Qi was appointed to succeed him. Due to the increasing number of students, an additional dormitory was built, and personnel were sent to the Philippines, Java, and other ports to solicit donations. The result was that the donations received were not very large after expenses were deducted. A library was started but not completed. In the first month of the fifteenth year, the school building was again occupied by the Fengtian Army, and all the students moved to Shanghai again. First, they used the Second Normal School of Ximen, and then rented houses in Xinxin Lane in Dapuqiao to hold classes. In April, they moved back. On May 21st, the school's 20th-anniversary celebration was held, and a three-day entertainment was held to celebrate. In the summer of the sixteenth year, President Jiang resigned, and the National Government appointed President Zheng to succeed him, reorganizing it into the National Jinan University. The Nanjing Women's Department was also merged into Zhenru, and the scale began to become grand. On June 6th of the eighteenth year, the Overseas Chinese Education Conference was held at the school. Seventy-eight representatives from China and Siam, British, Dutch, French, and American territories attended. It lasted for seven days and nights, and forty-five resolutions were passed (published in the Nanyang Education Conference Report). Chinese and foreign educators gathered together to discuss education, which was a groundbreaking event in our country. This year, the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang also resolved to establish a board of directors to promote the school to become the highest overseas Chinese institution of the Three Principles of the People. It stipulated that there would be eleven directors and formulated regulations, which were approved by the Central Executive Committee and the Ministry of Education. As for construction, after the library was completed, Lian Yi Hall, the Science Hall, the Girls' Dormitory, the Faculty Dormitory, the Auditorium, the Junior and Senior High School Dormitories, the Middle School Classrooms, and offices were built in succession. In addition, thirteen small Western-style houses were built on the Jinan Village base and rented to faculty and staff for accommodation. In the planning stages are the gymnasium, etc., which will also begin construction soon. In addition, the Jinan Bank was established in the school, specializing in managing students' income and expenses. Currently, in addition to the middle school department, the university department has five colleges: Liberal Arts, Sciences, Law, Business, and Education, with a total of eighteen departments, as well as two specialized departments for diplomacy and teacher training. In addition, the free elementary school was changed to an experimental elementary school under the jurisdiction of the school. Overseas Chinese students from various regions come to study, with as many as one thousand three hundred people, and those coming from various ports are still coming in an endless stream. Unfortunately, due to the limited number of dormitories, it is temporarily impossible to accommodate them all. In addition, a Southeast Asian and American Cultural Affairs Department was specially established to communicate with overseas areas at any time, communicate news from China and Southeast Asia, and edit periodic magazines, Nanyang Research, which are mailed to various educational institutions overseas. A Nanyang Series has also been edited, and more than twenty types have been published! There are still more than thirty types being edited, which will be printed successively. Although the equipment is limited by funding and has not been fully completed, it is still barely sufficient for application. As for the library, there are already 33,050 Chinese and Western books. The graduates of each department are either working for the party and the country or serving the society. They are found in all walks of life, including the military, political, academic, and business circles. Those who are engaged in education in Southeast Asia are especially reputable, and various schools compete to recruit them. There are also many who have accumulated huge wealth in business and hold overseas economic power. In the domestic banking industry, such as the general manager of Shanghai Hefeng Bank, is a graduate of our school. Other banks, such as Xinhua Bank, also have students from our school. There are alumni associations in China, such as in Nanjing, Guangzhou, Shantou, Jiangxi, Jinan, Qingdao, and Wuhan, and there are also alumni associations abroad, such as in Siam, Yangon, Singapore, Kuala Lumpur, and Manila. This year, the Shanghai Alumni Association has asked President Zheng to allocate two acres of land in Zhenru for the construction of the association's headquarters. The drawings have been completed and will be built soon. In the future, it will be used for office work and to receive overseas Chinese who return to China. The sports department has already gained considerable honor in China, and in the seventeenth year and this year, it went south twice. The first time was to the Malay Peninsula, Siam, and Annam, and the second time was to the Philippines. The team also went to Guangzhou to compete. When competing in various ports overseas, it not only won many awards but also promoted the progress of sports in our country, causing foreigners to admire and increase the international status of our country, washing away the insult of being the "sick man of East Asia." Others have studied abroad and obtained doctoral degrees, practice law in Shanghai, and serve as teachers at their alma mater, while others are full-time teachers. There are also those who are studying abroad and have not yet returned. Talented people are emerging one after another, which is the glory of our school. In this short period of time, the school's affairs have developed and achieved such great results, which can be said to be extremely commendable. However, President Zheng still believes that it is not enough. He also plans to move the middle school department back to Nanjing in order to expand it. He also plans to purchase hundreds of acres of land in Zhenjiang and other places to open a large farm and establish a complete agricultural science department on the spot to cultivate agricultural talents so that after completing their studies and returning to Southeast Asia, they will have rich knowledge and experience in cultivation and compete with other races in agriculture. If this is the case, then the future of our school will be bright and unlimited. I have been a member of this school for twelve years. I am ashamed of my own lack of talent and have made no contribution. Now, on the occasion of the twenty-fifth anniversary and the completion of the fourth anniversary of the university, I will write down what I know in a summary, hoping to commemorate this day. It is written in haste, and errors and omissions are inevitable. However, what I regret is that my former colleagues are now as rare as morning stars, which is a pity. Of those I meet every day, there are only three people now (two of whom have left the school once). The rest have either moved into politics and business or moved their desks elsewhere. Thinking of old friends, I can't help but think of the Wei River in the north and the Yangtze River in the east. However, compared to educators in the East and West, they do not consider education to be difficult and tirelessly devote themselves to it as a lifelong career, but their interests seem to be different. Some say that the social environment in our country is very different from that of other countries. Since the environment is different, it is difficult to force them to be the same. How can it be said that educators are fickle and have no perseverance? Is that so? Is it really so? I write this here to record my feelings.

Dean Chen Zhongfan of the College of Liberal Arts

Dean Yu Jitai of the College of Sciences

Dean Wang Renlin of the College of Law

President Zheng's Memorial Ceremony for Deceased Schoolmates in the Cemetery

Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, a public memorial ceremony was held in the school cemetery for the deceased schoolmates. Hundreds of people attended, and President Zheng presided over the ceremony (Secretary-General Fan Shouzhi stood in for him). Bao Shoukang gave a speech, saying that the commemorative ceremony was to celebrate the living and to remember the deceased. His speech went as follows:

"On the twelfth day of June in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, one day before the celebration of the twelfth five-year anniversary of our school's founding and the fourth anniversary of the university's establishment, President Zheng Hongnian, leading all teachers and students of the school, respectfully offers clear wine and ample offerings to the spirits of the deceased students in front of the cemetery, saying:

You students have come here, and your tombs are here. Your souls each have a resting place, some from the Lingnan mountains, others from the warm continents, each with a home. When you came here, you carried books and drums, like guests returning home. As the years changed, you hoped to achieve a little, and your ambitions were not small. But alas, you died tragically in Shanghai, and your wishes were not fulfilled. Your heroic hearts were sheathed, and your talents were confined to the corners of the courtyard, unable to take flight. The humble dwellings are desolate, the autumn and spring frosts and dews are heavy and unbright. The temporary structures are piled high, and words are separated by darkness and light, reaching only long sighs. Some of you were ill and died quickly by your bedsides. The land and people are different, and I know that it is so. The illness lies in the depths of reason. In the past, I adjusted the medicines, and was truly in charge. The heart was not to be pierced, the lungs withered like feathers, and life was not to be relied upon. Alas, you were promising, but you came to nothing, and I shed tears in secret. Orchids bloom in spring, not in autumn dew, who will take care of them? Some of you died without settling your lives, either by hanging yourselves or drowning yourselves. Your intentions were pure, and your meaning can be understood, fulfilling a small faith. Lonely Han Fei, sad Qu Yuan, did not learn to stretch and stretch. Throwing oneself from a cart to drink poison, cutting off the head and breaking the shin, rejecting people with death. Knowing life and death, one death cuts off everything, how can it be said to be returning to benevolence? The past is gone, the tomb door is closed, and I feel guilty and sad. Today, I come to worship. The shepherd's purse is sad in the wind, and the plum rain is dark. Looking at your neighbors, calling your companions, come to this meeting in time. Do you have any pain? Open your hands and feet, and look at your injuries. Are you homesick? Widen your sleeves, and embrace the spring breeze and warmth. On the occasion of this school celebration, the completion of four years, and the passing of twenty-five years. The sound of music rises, graceful and elegant, and many scholars line up. Cherishing old friendships, I alone face a corner, and my joy is about to fall. Raising banners and sending condolences, to settle your spirits. The sound of the ritual is solemn. Alas, come, you students, all around me. Your sadness is my sadness, your joy is my joy, I see you as if you were wounded. I am like your father, and you are like my children, how can I not be hurt? I offer this clear wine, which can reach the nine springs, may you come and enjoy it."

Zheng Hongnian's Announcement

Our school is holding a celebration for the 25th anniversary of the school's founding and the 4th anniversary of the university's establishment, as well as a graduation ceremony, achievement exhibition, and entertainment, etc. We are grateful to the ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life who have graced us with their presence to observe the ceremonies and visit everything. Due to the large scale of the school, there may be some inadequacies in the reception. We ask for your understanding and extend our sincere thanks.

Dean Yu Jitai of the College of Sciences

All Kinds of Middle School Department News

1. The middle school department has recently published the following three kinds of publications:

1. A Glance at the Middle School Department: Contains the general situation of the middle school department, the curriculum schedule of each subject, various regulations, various certificate formats, and a summary of form book formats.

2. Middle School Department Curriculum Outline: Contains the objectives, outlines, textbooks, and reference books of each subject.

3. A List of Past Graduates and Current Students of the Middle School Department: Divided into two parts, past graduates and current students, each containing their names, native places, ages, places of residence, etc., in great detail. The above three publications are all placed in the middle school department's visitor lounge and distributed to visitors.

2. The middle school department has a monthly magazine, which is published every month. Recently, another issue has been released.

3. The middle school department's normal science department has published Overseas Chinese Education. The fourth issue, which was released last month, is also placed in the middle school department's lounge and distributed to all visitors

4. The achievement room is the place to display students' academic achievements. Since the middle school department's achievement room was established in early April, it has not promoted extravagance, but only sought reality. Therefore, most of what is displayed are full class test papers. Recently, they have intensified their work and collected student achievements, which is extremely busy. I hope that visitors will give practical criticisms to improve.

5. The middle school department has made preparations for receiving guests at the commemorative meeting. First, paper signs are placed at the crossroads entering the school gate and in front of the middle school department's office, stating the general situation of the middle school department, so that visitors can understand it at a glance. Second, there are signposts and greeters from the school gate to various parts of the middle school department to facilitate visitors' visit.

Glimpses of Entertainment

Yesterday was the third day of our school's anniversary celebration. The various exhibition halls were open as usual. Entertainment parties were held in the afternoon and evening. Although the weather was hot, no less than a thousand people from nearby residents and local ladies and gentlemen went to visit. There were many wonderful performances in the program, such as "Love" directed by writer Gu Zhongyi, as well as excellent dances by female students, operas, Peking Opera by the Peking Opera troupe, and martial arts by the martial arts troupe, which were very popular. The Nanyang Homecoming and Model by the Overseas Chinese Student Federation were especially distinctive.

Exhibition Situation of the Biology Department at the Exhibition Site

(1) Specimen Manufacturing Room

(A) Location: No. 2 Science Hall

(B) Content: Contains over ten animals, including two white rats, two squirrels, four zebra finches, one canary, and one white-eye. There is also one slicer, one incubator, ten sets of instruments for making sliced ​​specimens, and three medicine cabinets.

(2) Plant Research Room

(A) Location: No. 3 Science Hall

(B) Content: One set of instruments for testing chemical action, two dissecting microscopes, one incubator, and over one hundred bottles of soaked plant specimens.

(3) Animal Research Room

(A) Location: No. 4 Science Hall

(B) Content: Dozens of species of bacteria that have been cultured, one hundred tubes of bacterial culture medium, one slicer and electric dryer, and a complete set of bacterial staining instruments.

(4) Instrument and Standard Product Display Room

(A) Location: No. 5 Science Hall

(B) Content: Two human models, two human skeleton models, dozens of physiological models, one hundred dissecting instruments, dozens of various animal skeletons, dozens of microscope accessories, and dozens of plant physiological experimental instruments, etc.

(5) Zoological Sequential Display Room

(A) Location: No. 6 Science Hall

(B) Content: There is a paper-covered tower, divided into five layers. Various animals are displayed on the top, and the top of the tower is a monkey. Then, in accordance with the order of biological evolution, it goes down step by step until it reaches the protozoa.

(6) Histology and Embryology Display Room

(A) Location: No. 7 Science Hall

(B) Content: Dozens of embryology and histology pictures are posted on the wall, and microscopes are placed on the table, totaling thirteen. Dozens of boxes of physiological sliced ​​specimens. Counting thousands of pieces.

(7) Plant Specimen and Marine Specimen Display Room

(A) Location: No. 8 Science Hall

(B) Content: Contains more than 500 bags of wheat seeds, more than 1,500 kinds of various plant wax leaf specimens, and more than 1,000 bottles of soaked marine specimens.

(8) Animal Specimen Display Room

(A) Location: No. 9 Science Hall

(B) Content: Dozens of mammals, more than 300 kinds of birds, and dozens of other kinds.

(9) Plant and Insect Specimen Display Room

(A) Location: No. 11 Science Hall

(B) Content: Dozens of anatomy diagrams are posted on the wall (because this room was originally an anatomy experiment room), the remaining types of plant specimens, and thousands of insect specimens.

(10) Lantern Room

(A) Location: No. 12 Science Hall

(B) Content: There is a lantern, which is placed with plant sliced ​​specimens, which are changed at any time, and there is also a written explanation.

As long as you do well, you don't have to care whether people know about it or not; (2) If you can have a plan and direction, small things will be successful, and if you extend it to big things, such as the mission that this school bears, you will definitely be able to achieve it.

Post-Marriage Musings

— (Fu Xuan)

——Encouraging Graduates and Inspiring Current Students——

Today marks the 25th anniversary of the founding of our school and the 4th anniversary of the completion of the university program. In terms of events, preparations have been extensive, with myriad ceremonies awaiting their commencement on the grand stage. In terms of literature, a commemorative album has been published to highlight the occasion, and reports from various departments will detail the events. We have nothing new to add here. However, amidst the grand celebration, there is also a supplementary graduation ceremony for the class of 1929. Graduates either continue their studies or enter the world. Let us set aside those who continue their studies for the moment. Those who enter the world are compared to a young woman leaving her maiden home. It is said, "When a maiden leaves her home, whether she meets a good or bad man determines her life. Whether her mother-in-law is kind or cruel affects her happiness. Once she returns home, she will have much to say to her sisters-in-law, brothers, and parents. Yet, she may not freely speak of her husband's shortcomings, but a harsh mother-in-law's stern face is easily seen. Thus, complaints are many, and pleasant stories are few, forced smiles are common, and tears are frequent. Only then does one realize how difficult it is to live in the world. One is either wounded by the treachery of human relationships or laments the futility of serving others. Leaving school and entering the world is much the same. Finding a job is like marrying a husband. Society is like the mother-in-law. In these times of economic hardship and youthful extravagance, few can fulfill their duties." I respond, "This is the situation of the past. Whether a maiden marries a good or bad man is ultimately predetermined. But those who leave school and enter the world today are like maidens who have been cast out, their future uncertain. They cannot find work, nor do they have a home to return to. Even if they find a place to perch, they must either compromise or use skills they did not learn. This leaves them feeling lost and empty. It is like the women of old, bound by etiquette and forced by harsh authority, who resigned themselves to their fate, inevitably leading to widespread complaints! Today's graduates may meet a good match and rejoice, or they may be forced to compromise, their faces filled with sorrow, or they may find no one to ask for advice, lamenting in empty rooms. Once they return to their alma mater, they will discuss worldly matters with their sisters and friends. Laughter, anger, scolding, tears, comfort, and complaints will mingle in the air. At this grand gathering, their emotions will be beyond description. Recalling the days of carefree ambition, cultivating oneself in solitude, cherishing harmonious friendships, and experiencing deep teacher-student bonds, they will be reluctant to leave the school gates again.

Although our experiences of joy and sorrow after leaving school differ, and our emotions vary accordingly, there are several things that must be clearly understood. The current Chinese society is unstable, riddled with problems. The distress of young people is immeasurable, and the difficulty of finding a way out is beyond words. Ultimately, this is due partly to the nature of society and partly to their own confusion:

Those who have experienced the world can describe in detail the ugly face of society. To seek a position, flattery and fawning are the prerequisites, and currying favor is the path to advancement. The shrewd criticize this as being lowly and subservient, while the upright scold it as being pedantic and impractical. Those who hold ideals and strive for integrity often find themselves lost and uncertain, unable to use their talents. As a result, resentment arises at home, criticism is leveled at society, and highly educated unemployed individuals dare not defend themselves. The so-called summoning of talent and welcoming of the worthy have disappeared today.

Even if one happens to find an opportunity, one is constantly fearful of losing it. Those who work diligently are ridiculed by their colleagues for "seeking favor." Those who are occasionally negligent are scolded by their superiors for "neglecting their duties." The mediocre are laughed at by their colleagues for being useless. The capable are pushed aside by both superiors and subordinates. Friendship turns into enmity, and relatives become like fire and water. Those seeking positions at the door are constantly slandered by those seeking to replace them. Moreover, people's minds differ, each as unique as their face. They praise outwardly but scheme inwardly. We are thus lost in a fog, unable to predict whether fortune or misfortune awaits us. The difficulty of working is thus evident. What is described above is only a fraction of the reality! As for the darkness of society and the decline of morality, it is extremely difficult to remain untainted. One is enticed by one thing and chased away by another. Bad habits become ingrained, which is truly lamentable. This ugly face of society leaves us in a difficult situation.

(2) Few current students are aware of the hardship of farming, and many are accustomed to extravagant lifestyles. They often believe that creating things in society is easy. They enjoy empty rhetoric and disdain practical skills. They even build castles in the air, believing that upon graduation, they will immediately ascend to high positions, like Gao Yao, sitting in high halls, displaying their glory to the world. Once they enter the world, they find a completely different path. Those in lowly positions are unwilling to compromise, while those with great responsibilities are unable to bear the burden. Moreover, they are using skills they did not learn, resulting in great effort and little effect! As a result, the dejected become passive, and the radical become extreme. Society becomes more chaotic, and it becomes more difficult to advance or retreat. This is one responsibility that we ourselves must bear.

Within the dormitory, it is like an inn. Those who skip classes boast of being "detached," while those who study diligently are ridiculed as being "bookworms." "Fashion" is their dream, and "pleasure" is their ideal paradise. Once they leave school and find employment, they find it dry and uninteresting, unable to settle into their jobs, or they lack specialized skills and are unable to handle tasks effectively, forcing them to resort to deception and trickery in the hope of survival. As a result, the strong become arrogant, and the weak are broken. Society becomes more chaotic, and it becomes more difficult to advance or retreat. This is another responsibility that we ourselves must bear.

Now that you have gathered here, your perceptions and feelings may not be exactly as described above, but the aforementioned aspects are undeniable features of the ugly face of society. Although the past is gone, the future can be improved. Graduates, having experienced hardship, should not bear to see current students repeat their mistakes. They should offer advice based on their experiences to prepare them for what lies ahead. This is also the purpose of the post-marriage advice upon returning home. Therefore, I would like to encourage the current students:

"Many of you are still unmarried, waiting to be betrothed. In a few years, whether you will leave home in marriage or be cast out is still unknown. However, the ways of the world must be understood. Society is turbulent, and human nature is unpredictable. How should you prepare to respond and advance? To avoid being criticized for being impulsive or feeling lost? How should you motivate yourselves in your studies and career choices? To avoid being incompatible with your roles and exhausted by your work? So that you do not end up washing your hands and entering the kitchen, unfamiliar with your mother-in-law's tastes."

I graduated not long ago and stayed at the school to serve. It is like a married woman returning to her maiden home, not yet having left her own door. I have only experienced a fraction of the hardships of the world. My shallow words may be laughed at by those in the know. But moved by my feelings, I have described them in detail as a filler for the commemorative publication. June 14th

Concurrently serves as the middle school principal, Mr. Hong Kui

News from the Executive Committees of the Commemorative Preparatory Committee

Origins of the First Executive Committee

The commemorative meeting of our school has four executive committees responsible for different aspects. The First Executive Committee is responsible for editing the commemorative collection of essays and the school overview, printing and distributing commemorative postcards and commemorative daily publications. The Second Executive Committee is responsible for the achievement exhibition of the university department. The Third Executive Committee handles matters related to the ceremony and entertainment. The Fourth Executive Committee is responsible for the achievement exhibition of the middle school department, etc. The First Executive Committee's collection of essays includes inscriptions from prominent figures of the party and the nation, contributions from various sectors, and essays by the school's faculty and staff. The school overview includes dozens of articles on various regulations, charts, and statistics. However, due to the tight schedule and time constraints for editing, brevity is unavoidable. We sincerely apologize for any shortcomings and hope that those with abilities will help to fill in the gaps and revise the text.

A Glimpse of the Second Executive Committee

Origins: This Executive Committee is in charge of achievement exhibition matters, which is one of the most interesting and most difficult tasks of the commemorative meeting. Although our school has been established for twenty-five years, it has only been reorganized into a university for four years. Thanks to the diligent planning of President Zheng and the support and assistance of people from all walks of life, we have been studying diligently day by day. However, our achievements are not comparable to those of renowned and advanced universities at home and abroad. Nevertheless, we dare not keep our knowledge to ourselves. We take this opportunity to contribute our knowledge and seek guidance and criticism from educational leaders and people from all walks of life, so that we can use it as a spur to improve. This is what this Executive Committee hopes for.

Personnel: This Executive Committee is headed by the deans of all colleges and the head of the registration department, with the full participation of all faculty and students of the university department.

Location: The location of the achievement exhibition was originally in the library. This building has three floors and forty rooms, and is located in the center of the school, surrounded by flowers and trees, with a gentle breeze. Today, All Sectors Hold Meetings to Commemorate the Passing of the Premier

Held at the City Party Headquarters at 9:00 AM

Today (the 16th) is the ninth anniversary of the Premier's martyrdom in Guangzhou. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters has specifically scheduled a commemorative meeting to be held today at 9:00 AM in the Grand Auditorium on the third floor of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters on Lin Yin Road in the South City. The City Executive Committee issued a statement to the public yesterday, saying,

Studying Methods for Sino-Japanese Cooperation

The National Goods Association Holds a Scheduled Meeting

The China National Goods Maintenance Association sent a letter to various organizations yesterday, saying, "Respectfully, since Japan has imposed a heavy tax of 100% on Chinese goods, millions of farmers, industrialists, and merchants in our country who rely on exporting to Japan and South Korea have been deprived of their livelihoods, displaced, and in dire straits. Our association has repeatedly joined forces with domestic and foreign organizations, promoted equality, and exchanged letters and telegrams, calling for rescue. However, Japan's ambition is rampant, and the effect is equal to zero. After the National Government unified the country and laid the foundation, our diplomatic authorities negotiated with Japan again and again, and finally signed the Sino-Japanese Agreement in May of the 19th year of the Republic of China, reducing the heavy tax by 30%, which is 70%. The agreement was for a period of three years, ending in May of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Our association believes that agreements between countries must be based on the principle of equality and mutual benefit. Today, the transportation of goods to China and the transportation of Chinese goods to Japan are taxed unequally, which is a major obstacle. Therefore, Japanese goods can be sold smoothly in China, while Chinese goods are still difficult to transport to Japan and South Korea.

This kind of pain must be fundamentally eradicated to save the lost rights and maintain the livelihood of the industrial and commercial sectors engaged in foreign trade. Therefore, on the 7th of the lunar month last month, we telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting permission to convene relevant organizations to study and amend the Sino-Japanese Agreement and submit it to the ministry for adoption. After review, on the 15th, we received a telegram from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating, "I have received your telegram of the 1st. Regarding the tariff rate for Chinese goods imported into Korea in the future after the current agreement expires, you may convene relevant organizations to study how to propose amendments and submit them to the ministry for consultation with the Ministries of Finance and Industry for review and handling. A special telegram is sent in reply. Ministry of Foreign Affairs (seal)." In view of this, we believe that the agreement is of great importance to our country's economy and people's livelihood. Now that the agreement period is about to expire, we should pool our wisdom and efforts to study new agreement methods and cooperate to proceed, so that we can gather wisdom and benefit, and avoid digging wells when thirsty and repeating the same mistakes. Therefore, we have specifically scheduled a joint meeting of various organizations to be held at 3:00 PM on the 23rd of this month at our association's office on Nine Acres of Land in Shanghai to discuss and study various concrete methods for the Sino-Japanese Agreement in order to proceed properly. At the meeting, the full text of the Sino-Japanese Agreement printed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will be distributed so that each article can be studied. At that time, we earnestly request that your office, association, or guild send representatives to attend and participate in the discussion and express your opinions for public resolution and implementation. We are deeply grateful for your prompt and active participation. With best wishes for your well-being."

Public Works Department Permits Resumption of Business for Domestic Goods Department Store

Results of Negotiations by the Bureau of Industry and Commerce

However, the Department Store is Unwilling to Open Automatically

The China United Domestic Goods Department Store has been closed by order of the Public Works Department for seven days and remains closed. After the Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent officials to negotiate, the Public Works Department has agreed to allow it to resume business. However, the department store itself is unwilling to open automatically. The various developments of yesterday are recorded below:

Negotiation Process: After receiving instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the Bureau of Industry and Commerce sent officials to thoroughly investigate the facts of the Domestic Goods Department Store. Subsequently, Li Zejin was dispatched to the Public Works Department to negotiate with the Director-General, Mr. Fessenden. The day before yesterday, together with the Director-General of the Public Works Department, Mr. Fessenden, Municipal Advisor Wu Jingxiong, Deputy Director He Dehui, and representatives from the Fire Brigade's Engineering Department, they went to the department store to inspect the various facilities. As a result, the Public Works Department agreed to allow the department store to resume business, but stipulated that the equipment in the amusement section must be completely improved. Yesterday, the Bureau of Industry and Commerce sent Pan Zengyin and Ji Zejin to the department store for further discussions. Because the Public Works Department had sealed the doors, the department store insisted that the Public Works Department should also be the one to open them and refused to open automatically.

A Discussion: Yesterday at 2 PM, Chinese members of the Public Works Department, Yu Qiaqing, and Chairman of the Ratepayers' Association, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jilong, and Standing Committee Member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Wang Yansong, invited Zhen Yulian from the Domestic Goods Department Store to a discussion. Yu and others stated that the department store should immediately resume business, and they would be responsible for handling all negotiations regarding losses. However, Mr. Zhang argued that the Public Works Department's illegal use of force was related to the business security of Chinese ratepayers within the concession. Until the principles of fairness, law, and responsibility for enforcement and handling were clarified, it would be inappropriate to open the doors without authorization, resulting in little progress in the discussion. It was agreed that further discussions would be held the day after tomorrow.

Reply to the Public Works Department: Yesterday, the Domestic Goods Department Store sent a letter to the Public Works Department, stating: "In reply to your letter No. 1121 of June 13th, regarding the letter sent by Mr. Zhang Deyin, Director of the Amusement Section of this department store, on June 4th, we have fully understood its contents. We hereby reply in detail and request your attention: (1) This department store is a department store engaged in the business of domestic goods. Apart from needing a license for the attached amusement section, this department store does not need to obtain a license according to your department's regulations, and there is no violation of regulations. The Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun companies also have attached amusement sections. Even if the amusement sections of the aforementioned three companies violate regulations, your department can only exercise its powers over their amusement sections and cannot stop the entire business operations due to violations in the amusement sections. (2) If your department believes that the attached amusement section of this department store violates regulations, according to the regulations of the license issued by your department, you can only stop the business of the amusement section, preventing tourists from buying tickets to enter. You cannot close its doors, cut off its access, and should not, without an order from the competent court, arbitrarily stop the entire business operations of this department store, close all the iron gates, and cut off its access. From this, it can be seen that your department's actions this time not only exceed the scope but also show contempt for the Chinese court, violate agreements, and infringe upon the court's authority. (3) The location of the attached amusement section of this department store is the same as the former New World before May 1st, which was approved and licensed by your department. The original equipment for handling amusement activities, like the New World, has not been changed, and the amusement activities have not been interrupted. There has been no time for changes. Why is it that your department considered the former New World satisfactory and issued a license, while you consider the amusement section with the same equipment attached to this department store unsatisfactory and refuse to issue a license? Furthermore, this department store took over the former New World based on its possession of a license that your department considered satisfactory and permitted to operate an amusement business. Now, your department suddenly expresses dissatisfaction with the attached amusement section of this department store. The responsibility for this inability to make a clear decision should be borne by your department. (4) Your department's letter states that the various changes proposed by your department are to protect the safety of the public's lives and property. Protecting the safety of the public's lives and property is your department's responsibility and a responsibility that your department must not neglect; otherwise, it would lose the original intention of all taxpayers setting up your department. This meaning and responsibility have a long history and should, of course, be consistent and identical before and after May 1st. Therefore, the New World amusement license issued by your department before May 1st should be the same as the amusement license issued to the amusement section attached to this department store after May 1st, paying careful attention to protecting the safety of the public's lives and property. Otherwise, it would be a violation of duty and bear corresponding responsibility. According to this, your department must have carefully considered and been very serious when issuing the amusement license to the former New World before May 1st, recognizing that all its equipment was completely legal and satisfactory before issuing the license. Why is it that after May 1st, you say that the same equipment is illegal and unsatisfactory? This is no different from your department stating that the previous issuance of the license was negligent, or that the safety of the public's lives and property before May 1st did not need to be protected. Upon investigation, your department's letter is a reply to the public letter sent by Mr. Zhang Deyin, Director of the Amusement Section of this department store, on June 4th, indicating that your department did not think there was no room for discussion in the June 4th letter and felt it was necessary to reply. This reply should have been made by your department before using force to order the closure on June 9th and should not have been delayed until June 13th. Furthermore, after this department store signed a contract to take over the former New World on April 20th, the Director of the Amusement Section, Mr. Zhang Deyin, applied to your department for a license transfer on April 28th. At that time, your department sent two Chinese constables, Nos. 632 and 709, and two fire brigade managers to the venue for management and allowed business operations. Even if there were unsuitable internal facilities, there should have been no risk of danger, and a reply discussing and studying Mr. Zhang's letter of June 4th should have been made. Your department did not do this. Your department's actions on June 9th are truly perplexing. Your department's letter states that completing the equipment for the various changes proposed by your department is a condition for this department store to open for business. However, this department store was closed by your department's illegal use of force, which is a matter of the business security of Chinese taxpayers. Therefore, until the principles of fairness, law, and responsibility for enforcement and handling are clarified, we dare not make any statements. This is our special reply."

Group Assistance: Yesterday, organizations such as the Shanghai National Goods Factories Association, the Woodworking Industry Union, the Pollen Industry Guild, and the West City Business Community Association submitted petitions to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting negotiations or sending letters to the department store expressing unified assistance (original text omitted).

Declaration by the Press and Labor Unions: To all public organizations, newspaper offices, elders, brothers, sisters, and compatriots throughout the country: Since the May 30th Massacre occurred in our country, the entire nation has been indignant at the frequent foreign insults and eager to wash away the humiliation, but without a way to do so. Everyone believes that the only way to save the country is to promote domestic goods to resist imperialist economic aggression. The Domestic Goods Factories in Shanghai, in view of this, pooled their efforts to organize the China United Domestic Goods Department Store, hoping to promote domestic goods and recover rights. However, the authorities in the concession, knowing that the development of the department store is detrimental to imperialism, deliberately try to destroy it at every opportunity. This time, the China National Goods Department Store, in order to expand its scope, moved its business from the former site of the Municipal Council on Nanjing Road to the new boundaries of the concession. The Public Works Department dared to create difficulties again and again, refusing to issue a license, and on the 9th of this month, it completely sealed off the department store and beat several employees, including Zhu Qiguang and Huang Xiliang. Such wanton destruction not only disregards our national sovereignty but also violates public law. Anyone with blood in their veins cannot but feel grief and indignation. The national goods movement is being promoted by the central government. The government has announced the recovery of legal rights in the concession. If this incident is not seriously negotiated, where is national sovereignty? Where is the law? We hope that compatriots across the country will quickly provide assistance. We will not give up until we receive a satisfactory response and compensation for losses. We hereby declare.

Yang Zhaoyun Visits Fessenden Regarding the Sealing of the Domestic Goods Department Store

The Department Store Section Can Be Opened

The Amusement Section Will Be Temporarily Closed

Since the China National Goods Department Store was suddenly closed by the police on the afternoon of the 9th, the citizens of Shanghai have been deeply surprised by this action of the Public Works Department, considering it to be inconsistent with legal procedures. Even if the department store has violated regulations, the Public Works Department should, in accordance with the agreement, file a public prosecution with the District Court of the Special Area, and the court should make a ruling according to law. It is not appropriate to close the store directly, which would exceed its authority and infringe upon the jurisdiction of our country's courts. Yang Zhaoyun, President of the District Court of the Special Area, believed that the Public Works Department and the District Court had always cooperated on everything, but this unfortunate incident occurred, which was regrettable. Especially since this matter concerns the rights of citizens and the authority of the court, in order to avoid escalating the dispute, he took the initiative to question and hoped for an early resolution. He expressed his opinions to the Public Works Department's legal representative. The Public Works Department's legal representative could not intervene due to limitations of authority. President Yang personally visited the Public Works Department yesterday to meet with Director-General Fessenden to protest in person and request the immediate opening of the store. Mr. Fessenden said that he also recognized that this action was not without error, but stated that he and the Board of Directors had not been informed of it beforehand. As for the National Goods Department Store section, it can be opened immediately and operate as usual, but the amusement section must wait until the fire exits and other equipment are complete due to incomplete facilities and the nature of fire hazards before it can be reopened. President Yang immediately stated that the entire store must be opened. If there are violations of regulations, they can be transferred to the court for handling. Mr. Fessenden said that he had no authority to allow this, but he could report this to the Board of Directors for discussion and remedial measures, which should not be difficult to resolve satisfactorily. He also said that he would convene a temporary Board of Directors meeting this afternoon (the 15th) to expedite the conclusion of this matter. President Yang believed that Mr. Fessenden's reply was sincere and took his leave. Later, it was heard that the temporary Board of Directors meeting was not convened yesterday and has been changed to Wednesday (the 17th). Therefore, this matter will likely be resolved after the Board of Directors meeting tomorrow. The National Goods Department Store will hopefully be opened as early as the 18th.

Fessenden Discusses the Reasons for Closing the Domestic Goods Department Store

Stating It Was to Protect the Safety of Citizens' Lives

At approximately 3:30 PM yesterday, the reporter met with Fessenden, Director-General of the Public Works Department, at the department's office. Mr. Fessenden made the following statements regarding the recent closure of the National Goods Department Store: The following is Mr. Fessenden's statement:

"Since the National Goods Department Store was closed, the general reports in the newspapers have been quite different from the facts. From beginning to end, the Public Works Department not only has no intention of opposing national goods but also believes that national goods are of good quality and low price and should be actively promoted. However, promoting national products is one thing, and ensuring the safety of the lives of general customers is another thing. The two must not be confused. I recall that when the National Goods Department Store was opened in the Municipal Council building, there were many flammable materials stored in the store. The Fire Brigade of this department negotiated with Mr. Zhang, the person in charge of the store, several times, informing him of the reasons for the ban and giving him a considerable deadline to make changes in accordance with the regulations, but he ultimately ignored them. After the store moved to the New World, the situation became even worse. In addition to the department store, there were also amusement parks and movie theaters, and the safety equipment in them did not comply with the regulations stipulated by this department. If an accident occurs (such as a fire), there will be many tourists in the venue, and hundreds of lives will be lost. In order to protect the safety of the lives of citizens, how can this department ignore the dangerous situation and fail to take measures to correct it in advance? This is the reason for the closure of the store. The current intention of this department is that the National Goods Department Store can be allowed to operate first, but the amusement section must wait until the fire exits and other facilities are complete before it can be restored."

Ministry of Communications Proclamation Prohibits Ships from Docking at the Yangzi Wharf

Due to Yang Ocean Company's Failure to Pay Rent

Ships Docking Will Not Be Cleared Through Customs

According to the New Sound News Agency, the National Government's Ministry of Communications has announced that the Shanghai Yangzi Wharf in Pudong, Shanghai, owned by the Ministry and leased to the Japanese Ocean Company, has violated the contract by delaying rent payments. The Ministry has notified the company of its cancellation of the lease on the 6th of this month and has also informed the Ministry of Finance to instruct the Jianghai Customs Commissioner to prohibit all Chinese and foreign ships from docking at the wharf from the 11th of this month. Yesterday, the New Sound News Agency reporter specifically visited the Jianghai Customs, the Port Authority, the Western assistant responsible for managing ships, and the general manager of the Ocean Company, Japanese national Funakoshi Shinjiro, to inquire about the customs' management of the wharf and the company's attitude toward the Ministry of Communications' announcement. Details are recorded below:

Ministry of Communications Proclamation: To notify the public, the Shanghai Pudong Yangzi Wharf belongs to the Ministry. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the wharf was leased to the Japanese merchant Ocean Company, and a contract was signed for both parties to abide by. However, the company failed to comply for long and delayed rent payments. Over the years, the arrears have been substantial. Despite repeated negotiations, the company has ignored them and repeatedly made excuses for delays. In order to protect property rights, the Ministry must cancel the lease according to the contract and completely recover the wharf. During this period, all Chinese and foreign ships must not dock at the wharf. In addition to notifying the company and consulting the Ministry of Finance to instruct the Jianghai Customs Commissioner not to clear customs for Chinese and foreign ships docking at the wharf from June 11th of this year, we are afraid that it will not be widely known, so we hereby announce.

Port Authority Attitude: According to a certain Western gentleman who assists in ship management at the Jianghai Customs Port Authority, he has not received any orders from the Jianghai Customs Commissioner regarding this matter prohibiting Chinese and foreign ships from docking at the wharf or denying customs clearance. He has only seen this advertisement in the newspaper. As for whether the Ministry of Finance has issued any instructions to the Jianghai Customs regarding this matter, he does not yet know. Therefore, the management of the Port Authority is still the same as for other wharves.

Ocean Company's Statement: The reporter then investigated the Ocean Company's general manager, Mr. Funakoshi Shinjiro. The general manager first told the reporter the history of the wharf, saying that the Yangzi Wharf was originally the property of the Germans. During the European War, because China also participated, the wharf became Chinese property after the European War. The Ocean Company signed a lease with the Chinese Beijing government around 1922 and signed a contract in 1923. Officials in the division could not be sure which property rights belonged to, so the rent could not be paid. However, it has been sent to a certain bank for deposit on a monthly basis. It will be paid immediately after the property owner is clear. The reporter then asked whether the Ministry of Communications had sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance to instruct the customs to prohibit Chinese and foreign seagoing ships from docking at the wharf, whether the company needed to request negotiations with the Japanese ambassador, and the amount of the accumulated rent and the name of the bank where it was deposited. He replied that there was no need to request negotiations with the Japanese ambassador on this matter. The company only sent people to consult with the Ministry of Communications. The total amount of arrears is about 500,000 taels, and the name of the bank where it is deposited cannot be disclosed.

Shashi Radio Station to Be Able to Communicate Nationally in Three Weeks

New Motors for Xuzhou and Guiyang to Be Shipped Soon

Page 14

Page 4

The International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications is planning to establish stations in various regions to expand the domestic radio network. Recently, the locations for setting up stations for communication have been confirmed to be Shashi, Xuzhou (Sichuan Province), and Guiyang. The new motor for the Shashi radio station, consisting of twenty-four boxes, has already been shipped. Yan Zhonglin, the chief engineer of the Shashi radio station appointed by the Ministry of Communications, set off yesterday for Shashi to direct the installation of the station. According to Wu Guixiang, director of the bureau, who spoke to a reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday, communication between Shashi and radio stations across the country can be realized in three weeks. The new motor for the Xuzhou radio station is currently being installed and will be shipped to Xuzhou in two weeks. The motor for Guiyang will be shipped out in four or five days.

Fisheries Bureau Officially Established Yesterday

Director Han Yougang Sworn into Office

The Fisheries Administration Bureau of Jiangsu and Zhejiang officially established yesterday. Director Han Yougang has also arrived at the bureau to take office and held a swearing-in ceremony at 3 PM yesterday afternoon. Zhao Jinqing, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, supervised the ceremony. Details are recorded below:

Representatives from Various Parties: Those who attended yesterday included Zhao Jinqing from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Wu Huanru representing the Bureau of Social Affairs, Chen Yanin representing the Consolidated Tax Bureau, Ding Shuhua representing the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, Liu Shiru from the Trademark Bureau, Ju Zhijing representing the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Special Area Court, and Wu Tinghua and Wang Wentai representing various fisheries experimental stations, totaling over 40 people.

Details of the Swearing-In Ceremony: (1) The Vice Minister takes his place; (2) The person being sworn in takes their place; (3) Everyone stands at attention; (4) Bow three times to the Party, the national flag, and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; (5) The Vice Minister respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will; (6) The Vice Minister supervises, and the person being sworn in raises their right hand and reads the oath; (7) The Vice Minister's instruction; (8) The Director's response; (9) Photograph.

Director's Oath: Director Han's oath stated, "I, Han, solemnly swear that I will abide by Sun Yat-sen's will, obey the Party's principles, abide by the laws, be loyal and diligent in my duties, never waste a single penny, never use a single person improperly, and never engage in private gain, corruption, or bribery. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment. This is my oath."

Vice Minister's Instruction: After the Director took the oath, Zhao Jinqing, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, delivered an instruction, briefly stating, "Our country's fisheries have always been freely operated by fishermen and merchants. The technology is immature, and few know how to improve it, so there cannot be good development. Moreover, there is exploitation by villains internally and aggression by the Japanese externally, so the future of fisheries is extremely perilous. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has specifically established a dedicated bureau for management in order to uphold Sun Yat-sen's teachings and promote fisheries. From now on, the protection and promotion of fisheries, and the prevention of foreign vessels from seizing resources, must be actively carried out. Director Han has abundant experience in fisheries, and I firmly believe that he can work hard to implement the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's purpose of promoting fisheries," etc. After the Vice Minister finished his instruction, the Director responded, briefly stating that he would abide by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's purpose and the Vice Minister's instruction and work hard in his duties.

Han's Brief Biography: Han Yougang is from Cixi, Zhejiang, 35 years old, and graduated from Soochow University. In the fourth year of the Republic of China, he worked in the press in Beijing, served as secretary to Wang Zhengting, and was the head of the accounting section of the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce. He is currently in this position. It is said that Han's family has been engaged in fisheries for three generations, and there is still a fish market in Shanghai.

Director's Remarks: After the ceremony yesterday, the reporter from the New Sound News Agency specifically asked about the bureau's future plans. It was mentioned that our country's fisheries lose approximately 50 million yuan each year. Liaoning and other places have been seized by Japanese fishermen and merchants, so the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has specially established four regional fisheries administrations: one in Fujian, two in Liaoning, three in Hebei and Shandong, and four in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The Jiangsu and Zhejiang region has been established today, and the other regions will also be established in order to promote fisheries. Regarding the implementation plan, in addition to security aspects, a special water police force has been dispatched to prevent bandits and eliminate pests in the fisheries. The most important thing is to improve the technology of fishermen, and the most difficult thing is that the knowledge of the current fishermen is too immature, so methods must be found to guide them and improve them. At the same time, in addition to catching natural fish, it is also planned to artificially cultivate fish to increase fishery production.

Taking Office Announcement: For the matter of announcement, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce issued order No. 170, stating, "Han Yougang is appointed as the Director of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fisheries Administration Bureau of this Ministry. This order includes a wooden seal of office with the inscription 'Seal of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Fisheries Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce,' etc. Upon receiving this order, the Director of this Bureau took office on May 1st and put the seal of office into use. In addition to reporting and notifying, this announcement is hereby made to inform fishermen, merchants, and all people."

Various Industries' Tax Regulations Committee Requests Exemption from Business Tax on Native Cloth

The Tax Regulations Research Committee of the various industry associations in this city sent a letter to the Municipal Finance Bureau yesterday, requesting exemption from business tax on the native cloth industry, stating: "Dear Sirs, we have investigated that the native cloth industry is a rare and small-scale handicraft industry in the country. Both the supply and demand sides are poor people. The National Government has resolved to exempt all taxes and levies. Even the customs duties that have been followed over the years were exempted by the Ministry of Finance on May 19th, regardless of whether they are shipped abroad or to areas where consolidated taxes have not been implemented, and the Customs Administration has ordered the Jianghai Customs Commissioner to comply. The business tax currently being drafted in this city does not specify a tax rate for this industry, nor does it specify an exemption. It seems that the main purpose of the National Government's exemptions from taxes and levies should be followed, and an explicit tax exemption should be given so that there is something to follow when taxes are levied in the future. This is also in line with the principle of establishing a business tax to offset local losses from levies. According to the industry's appeal to the association, we are forwarding a letter to you, hoping that your bureau will approve an explicit exemption in order to maintain it. We would be most grateful. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau."

Shanghai County District Political Meeting Record

Fifteenth Session

The Shanghai County Government held its fifteenth district political meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Present were the heads of the six districts under the county, Wu Yingqing, Peng Zhaotang, Yang Fulin, Bi Huan, Ge Xiusheng, and Wang Chengyao, as well as County Secretary Ye Dezhen. County Chief Yan Shenyu chaired the meeting, with Hu Gongshou recording. The meeting commenced as scheduled, and the following resolutions were discussed and approved: (1) A proposal from the County Chief regarding how to allocate the special autonomous surtax levied under the deed tax item for the 20th year. It was resolved that: (A) The special autonomous surtax collected with the deed tax should be allocated and disbursed based on the amount of cultivated land in each district. (B) The special autonomous surtax collected with the broker's tax should be distributed equally to each district. (2) A proposal from the County Chief regarding how to expedite the submission of the 20th year budgets from each district. It was resolved that the budgets should be submitted by the end of June. (3) A proposal from the County Chief regarding the re-reporting of the office staff of each district office to the county for verification. It was resolved that each district should report to the county for record-keeping before July. (4) A proposal from the County Chief regarding compliance with the order from the Civil Affairs Department for each district to submit expenditure calculation statements. It was resolved that, starting from July, expenditure calculation statements and revenue-expenditure reconciliation statements should be prepared, along with receipts, and submitted to the county for verification and forwarding. (5) A proposal from the County Chief regarding how to regulate the implementation methods for distributing residence permits in each district. It was resolved that the program should commence on July 1st, with each district responsible for issuing the permits and each public security bureau assisting. The detailed implementation methods will be formulated separately.

The Bureau of Commodity Inspection and Testing Publishes "A Simple Explanation of Uniformity Testing of Raw Silk"

All countries pay attention to the uniformity of raw silk quality (commonly known as "Evenness"). In order to meet this requirement, Japan invented various silk reeling machines, such as the Omikawa type, to achieve uniformity in raw silk. At the same time, silk inspection stations also researched and developed methods and machinery for testing uniformity to assess the degree of uniformity and provide a basis for trade. Manufacturing and testing are considered together, and the great effectiveness can be seen in the situation of Japanese raw silk. The silk manufacturing machinery in our country's silk factories is extremely outdated, and inspection methods and equipment have not been given attention. Although improvements are gradually being made now, there is no clear direction on how to set them up. In view of this, the Raw Silk Inspection Department of the Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection and Testing has specially compiled a booklet entitled "A Simple Explanation of Uniformity Testing of Raw Silk," explaining the structure of the machinery, its operation methods, and the inspection procedures, etc. Yesterday, it was distributed to various silk factories, and a circular was sent to various trade associations to notify all factories to pay attention.

The Bureau of Commodity Inspection Starts Testing Sugar Yesterday

Recently, the Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection and Testing has added a lot to the commodity inspection, such as raw silk, tung oil, wool, etc. Starting yesterday, it has also added sugar inspection. All sugar merchants who import must report to the bureau to send personnel to inspect. Sugar is divided into nine types, from two and a half Wen to four and a half Wen. The bureau has set the standard for sugar types, which is based on Dutch sugar. The inspection fee is two cents per dan. Zhou Da Yao and Wu Zhuo, two technical officials, are in charge.

Inauguration of the Joint Righteousness Branch Standing Committee

The Shanghai Joint Righteousness Society was organized by the late Mr. Sun Yat-sen. Throughout its history, it has repeatedly made contributions to the party and the country. Recently, due to the long absence of the standing committee members, the society's affairs were chaotic and difficult to stop. Now, Tang Hai'an, the current Jianghai Customs Supervisor, has been publicly elected to take over the management of the association's affairs. The inauguration ceremony was held at 3:00 PM on the 14th, with about 60 guests present, creating a grand occasion for a while.

Year-End Half-Month Bonus for the Two Railway Lines

After the Shanghai-Nanjing and Nanjing-Hangzhou Railway Bureaus ordered their respective departments to prepare lists for the year-end half-month bonus for the 19th year for the workers and employees on the two railway lines, the clerks on the two lines jointly submitted a request to the Railway Bureau a few days ago, stating that since they are all serving on the railway, although the positions are divided into internal and external, the responsibilities are the same. Moreover, there has never been any outstanding treatment in the past. How can we clearly distinguish between them?
