Declaration of Silk Workers' Demand to Restore Wages

The Shanghai Sixth and Fourth District Silk Industry Union and the Preparatory Committee of the Special Zone Silk Industry Union, etc., issued a declaration yesterday regarding the issue of restoring the original wages of female workers, stating that since the wages of our industry were stipulated by contract between labor and capital in 1927, they have been mutually observed. Until October of last year, at that time, due to the factory's operating losses, there was a discussion on temporarily reducing wages. The Social Bureau convened a mediation, and both parties sincerely negotiated. At that time, our labor side could not bear to see the factory's business bankrupt, which would affect the national industry, so we demonstrated the spirit of labor-capital cooperation and expressed twelve points of sincerity, willing to save on food and clothing and painfully agree to calculate wages at 85% of the original amount, until the end of May 1941. It was stated that after the expiration date, the wages would remain the same, and temporary implementation conditions were signed on file. Since the reduction of wages for seven months, the suffering of our labor side has been indescribable. However, we only endure the pain for a while, and we always hope that when the term expires, the capital side will naturally restore the wages as agreed, so that we can still maintain our lives. Unexpectedly, the term has now expired, and the capital side has repeatedly delayed the restoration of wages, with no sincerity at all. Such a situation is contrary to the spirit of labor-capital cooperation, and they only use the excuse that silk prices are low and they are unable to maintain the wages. However, we all know that when the wage reduction was negotiated last year, the average silk price was 720 taels, but now the silk price has exceeded 900 taels. Judging from their intentions, they are using all kinds of deceptive words to cover up the authorities' observation and achieve their selfish desires. The silk factory industry is the most numerous in Shanghai, followed by Wuxi. The wages in Wuxi were originally 58 cents, but since the wage reduction in Shanghai, they were also reduced to 53 cents (Shanghai only 51 cents). Until January of this year, they were paid as before. Compared with the living standards in Wuxi and Shanghai, there is no need to argue that everyone knows. Is the business in Wuxi different from that in Shanghai, or are the workers in Wuxi better than those in Shanghai? Now that the eight million silk industry public bonds are about to be issued, even if the capital side suffered losses last year, it will not be difficult to recover with this infusion. The capital side should consider the government's painstaking efforts to help the workers and take care of the workers' pain. They stubbornly refuse to restore the meager wages. I don't know what their intentions are. Now, most of the factories in Shanghai have stopped working. The reason is the lack of raw materials and hoarding, which has nothing to do with the issue of wage restoration. Now, in order to make a living, our workers are struggling to demand the restoration of wages, and we firmly express our determination to achieve our goals. Otherwise, we would rather sacrifice ourselves and there is no room for compromise. We hope that people from all walks of life will give us their sympathy and assistance, and we hope that the authorities will make a fair ruling. This is what the workers pray for day and night. We respectfully declare this and hope for your public consideration.

Residents Should Follow the New System of Weights and Measures

Notification from the Taxpayers' Association

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association issued a notice to the residents of the concession yesterday, advising them to follow the new system of weights and measures, stating the following: Regarding the matter of announcing and implementing the new system of weights and measures, we have received a letter from the Shanghai Municipal Government stating that the case of promoting the new system of weights and measures in this city has been repeatedly invited to the Special Zone authorities to hold meetings and discussions, and officials have been sent to attend. The deadline for completing the unification on the first day of this month is approaching. All vegetable markets have already scheduled to implement the new system first on June 1st. The Special Zone is related to the observation of China and foreign countries, and it is appropriate to promote it in a unified manner to establish a good reputation. We have always known that your association is a representative of the citizens, and you are particularly enthusiastic in urging and improving the administration of the Special Zone. We hereby send a special letter to you, hoping that you will assist in promoting the necessity of unifying weights and measures, so that it can be completed as scheduled. The unified system of weights and measures has been a unified need of the people since the Republic of China. The National Government has ordered a thorough unification, and the Weights and Measures Law was promulgated on February 16, 1929. The Ministry of Industry has stipulated the date of implementation in this city. Therefore, all people living within the territory of the Republic of China must abide by and follow it. Those who violate the relevant laws and regulations will be subject to sanctions according to law. Since the old system of weights and measures has been legally abolished, anyone who uses it again is committing a crime. Therefore, we hereby notify the residents of the concession that they should immediately comply with the new Weights and Measures Law. All rulers, dou measures, scales, etc., must be discarded and replaced with new ones as soon as possible. Legal rulers, dou measures, scales, etc., can be purchased from the Weights and Measures Inspection Office of the Xiejiao Manufacturing Bureau Road. Please do not wait and see and harm yourself. This announcement.

Brokerage Industry Requests Business License

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends a Letter Requesting to Determine the Location

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a letter from the Coal and Charcoal Trade Association requesting an explanation of the scope of the broker's tax and the location for applying for a business license. Yesterday, it sent a letter to the Business Tax Preparatory Office of the Municipal Finance Bureau, requesting it to consider the matter. The original text is recorded as follows: Dear Sir, on the 13th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Coal and Charcoal Trade Association, stating that according to the announcement of the Shanghai County Government, those who pay the brokerage tax will no longer pay the business tax, but must apply for a business license. In the future, will this business license be obtained on behalf of the Shanghai County Government, or will it be obtained directly from the Municipal Finance Bureau? Please investigate and indicate, etc. It has been reported to the association that the coal and charcoal industry has always obtained licenses and paid the brokerage tax. The reason for this question is that the brokerage tax belongs to the county, while the business license belongs to the city. The jurisdictions of the two are different, so there is this question. In the future, merchants who pay the brokerage tax should apply for a business license in accordance with Article 4 of the regulations. If the brokerage tax is collected by the County Finance Bureau and the business license is also forwarded by the County Finance Bureau, it seems to be too circuitous. Correspondingly, we have sent a letter for your consideration, and we ask your office to determine the method for transfer.

Jihe Steamer Damages Wooden Boat

Collision: The Jihe steamer of Jardine Matheson & Co., which returned to Shanghai from Hankou this time, stopped the ship to allow passengers to go ashore in Jiangyin at 1:00 AM on the 14th, as usual, and temporarily threw a river anchor. At that time, the Jihe had already stopped the ship, and was about to launch a sampan to transfer passengers ashore, but there was already a large private ship transporting wood there, commonly known as the "duck butt boat," transporting wood from Shanghai to the Fairy Temple in Yangzhou, which had anchored in Jiangyin for the night. The Jihe steamer was impacted by the upstream water, the ship moved, and hit the wood-transporting boat horizontally. The wooden boat could not avoid it, and the bow was violently hit by the Jihe steamer, and it was immediately destroyed. Fortunately, the ship was huge and was not sunk, but the head was severely damaged. The iron railing and four iron support columns on the left side of the Jihe steamer were also broken, which shows the intensity of the collision. Fortunately, there were no injuries at both boats entrance.

Compensation: After the Jihe caused the accident, the wood-transporting boat was seriously damaged, and the wooden boat was anchored when it was hit by the Jihe. The responsibility lies with the British ship. The owner of the wooden boat negotiated with the Jihe captain, Law Huier, requesting compensation for the loss. The Jihe ship owner first inspected the collision situation and the extent of the damage, and accommodated the wood boat owner's request. He accompanied the owner of the wood transport boat to Shanghai on the Jihe steamer, reported the matter to the Westerners of the company, first repaired the damaged iron railing support columns of the Jihe, and exported as usual this morning, and sent personnel to inspect the damage of the wooden boat and estimate the compensation.

Recent Banditry and Hail Disasters in Henan

Report Obtained by the Jisheng Association

The China Jisheng Association recently received a telegram from Zhang Huizhen, Chairman of the Henan Relief Association, and others, stating that five places in Henan Province, including Guangluo and Gushang, have been ravaged by red bandits for a long time, who have committed arson, looting, rape, and murder, and have fled completely, mostly begging at the train stations in Xinyang, with no home to return to, barely surviving and hoping for rescue. Those who fled to Wuhan and Wan Ying and other places have reached tens of thousands, with death and displacement, the situation is extremely tragic. Recently, the Henan bandits were painfully suppressed by the army and fled to the mountainous areas of Song County and Nanzhao, where they burned and killed countless people. They also fled to Nanyang, northeast of the Guanxiang area, and set it on fire, killing thousands of people and looting more than 10,000 people. When the army arrived to disperse them, they attacked Tanghe again, gathered hundreds of babies, broke their brains and bellies, and used them as laughter. Nude women were forced to parade in the streets during the day. The atrocity of burning and killing was several times that of Xiangxi in the past. Fleeing to beg for their lives, they cannot live. Song County reported that on the evenings of May 30 and 31, there was wind and rain, and hailstones fell, as big as chicken eggs, lasting for two hours, accumulating more than a foot thick, extending about 30 li from east to west and 80 li from north to south, and no place was spared. The autumn seedlings were destroyed, and the wheat to be harvested was also seriously injured. Banditry and natural disasters have reached this point. Personnel were sent to investigate and the scene was unbearable. They are in deep water and fire, and are waiting to be rescued. They have repeatedly telegraphed for relief, hoping for rescue, which is a great merit. The heavenly disasters and bandit disasters in Henan Province are expanding day by day. The great catastrophe has reached today and it is really beyond saving. The Nanyang Gongzhen of the association has suspended work because the stonemasons and equipment were all looted by the bandits, but hopes that the ground will be slightly calm before proceeding with the work to complete the century-old water conservancy plan.

Obvious Adultery in the Shanghai West Assassination Case

A Male Corpse with Four Knife Wounds

The Penis Was Also Completely Cut Off

At about 8:45 AM yesterday, an anonymous male corpse was suddenly found assassinated in the wilderness near the Xiaoshadu Lime Kiln in Shanghai West. There were a total of four knife wounds all over the body. The strangest thing was that the deceased's penis was also cut off, and the situation was extremely tragic. The details are described as follows:

Murdered Male Corpse Found: The area behind the Xiaoshadu Lime Kiln in Shanghai West belongs to the jurisdiction of the Fourth and Sixth Districts. It is abnormally desolate. Therefore, there are only a dozen or so thatched sheds built by poor Jiangbei immigrants nearby, and pedestrians rarely visit. At about 8:30 AM yesterday, a murdered male corpse was suddenly found there. When nearby residents saw it, they were shocked and immediately ran to report to the patrolling police of the Fourth District. The police officers reported to the Sixth District Police Station, because the location belongs to the jurisdiction of the Sixth District. Patrol Captain Hu Lizhong reported to the Sixth District Headquarters.

Penis Completely Removed: After receiving the report, District Chief Ren immediately led Patrol Officer Xu Tao and Detective Liu Shaoqing to the scene to inspect it. It was found that the male corpse was about 30 years old, slightly pockmarked, wearing a gray serge long gown, lined with a white silk shirt and pants, and wearing serge round-toed shoes, barefoot and without socks. A small gauze melon-skin cap was discarded beside the corpse, and there were no other items beside it. The head was cut into a hole by a knife. In addition, there was a knife wound on the back of the neck and the left leg, each about an inch deep. What was strange was that the lower penis and testicles were completely removed, and the blood and flesh were blurred, and it was unbearable to look at. However, there were obvious blood stains left on the ground, so they followed the traces until the back of the Fuxin Third Factory in the Fourth District jurisdiction. It is estimated that the distance from the corpse is about 800 meters.

The Court Sends Personnel to Inspect: After District Chief Ren finished the inspection, he immediately ordered his subordinates to arrest the murderer within a limited time, and ordered the local Baojia to report to the local court for inspection. At about 3:00 PM, the court specially appointed Prosecutor Yang Wenjun to bring the clerk to the scene to verify the corpse. It was found that the anonymous male corpse was indeed murdered with a knife before his death. No family members were found, so he ordered the Baojia to report to the court for collection, pending the arrest of the murderer for investigation.

The Content Obviously Involves Adultery: Judging from the above situation, it is speculated that the deceased was neatly dressed, but why were only the two feet bare and wearing shoes? The murderer had already killed the deceased, thinking that the purpose had been achieved, but he must cut off the penis. The content contains adultery, which is obvious. Moreover, the starting point of the blood stains is behind the Fuxin Factory, which proves that the murderer killed the deceased and abandoned the body in a remote place, deliberately making it suspicious. Initially, it was unexpected that there were blood stains left on the way. Therefore, the cracking of this case is only a matter of time.

Her Husband Requests Cohabitation for Trial

After Being Released from Prison with No Place to Live, He Chopped His Own Head with a Knife

Xia Wengao Suffered a Major Nervous Breakdown

His Situation is Pitiable and His Circumstances Are Even More Tragic

Xia Wengao, a native of Yancheng, is 28 years old. He has always lacked a proper occupation and spent his days with low-class people, specializing in using extortion as a means. He considered that extortion and looting would not be a long-term plan, so he changed into a robber last year, specializing in robbing passers-by of their property on the road (commonly known as "killing pigs logically"), but unfortunately he was arrested by the police, sent to the court, found guilty and sentenced to imprisonment, and sent to the Jiangsu Second Prison of Caohejing for execution. Unexpectedly, after Xia entered prison, he suddenly suffered from a nervous illness, spoke incoherently, and acted abnormally. When his sentence expired the day before yesterday, after his release, he thought that he had nowhere to live, he was depressed, and his nervous illness suddenly broke out again. At about 3:00 PM, he rushed to the door of No. 77 Zhangjia Lane, Nanshi, where he lived, and said to Zhou San, a fellow villager who was a rickshaw puller, "My parents and brothers have always lived here with you. Now I want to see my parents." Zhou replied that his parents had moved to other places a long time ago. Xia heard this and left angrily. At about 6:00 AM yesterday, Xia rushed to Zhou's house again, without saying a word, suddenly took the kitchen knife placed on its　 and chopped his head fiercely. In an instant, blood flowed like a waterfall, he fell to the ground in extreme pain. Zhou was shocked to see this and immediately sent him to the hospital for treatment. After the doctor bandaged him, Zhou called the guard Liu Shaoyi from the 14th post and took him to the first sub-station of the first district, where the director conducted a preliminary interrogation. Xia confessed that he was desperate because he thought that his life was hopeless, so he had no choice but to chop his head with a kitchen knife, intending to commit suicide. When questioned, Zhou confessed that he was 41 years old, and that Xia's family had indeed lived in the same house with him before, but later, because of his improper behavior, he was afraid of future involvement, so he moved back to his hometown three years ago. Unexpectedly, Xia came to his house the day before yesterday and asked to stay with him, but because of his bad character, he refused on the spot, and he left, and today he suddenly came to cause this incident of self-chopping with a knife, etc. It was observed that Xia was suffering from a nervous illness and the documents immediately were submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for review.

At the beginning of spring, the association was chanting sutras with great enthusiasm, so Patrol Officer Liang diligently ordered them to stop the Dharma service and leave the association. The residents of the town heard the news and rushed to watch, and the road was blocked.

25th Anniversary Celebration of the Chinese Company of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps

Many Participants from All Walks of Life

The Chinese Company of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps held its 25th-anniversary celebration the day before yesterday at the shooting range barracks. A large number of people attended. National flags fluttered on the stage, and prizes were plentiful. The Chairman of the Public Works Department, Mr. MacNaghten, was absent due to illness and was represented by Deputy Chairman Mr. Xue Baojun. Other attendees included the Commander of the Volunteer Corps, Mr. Thomas, and his wife; the Chairman and Vice Chairman of the Chinese Company Association, Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Yuan Hengyun; the Commander of the French Garrison in Shanghai, Major Maguet; the Chief Inspector, Captain Martin; the Deputy Chief Inspector, Mr. Yang; the Deputy Commander of the Volunteer Corps, Mr. Marker; and former Chinese Company Commanders, Majors Xu and Hu, and former Headquarters Staff Officer, Mr. Ke Ning. First, a presentation ceremony was held for the regimental flag, which was publicly donated by Shanghai Chinese merchants, represented by Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, who praised the team's achievements. Then, Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Yuan Hengyun delivered speeches, briefly recounting the history of the team. Subsequently, Deputy Chairman of the Public Works Department, Mr. Xue Baojun, presented long-service medals and silver thread badges. Liu Jinghe, Chong Dihua, and Song Yunqi received double silver thread badges, Chen Huachu received a single silver thread badge, and Wang Weishen, Wang Yanqing, and Sheng Shaoming all received medals. Then, Lieutenant Li Yushu held the flag, and the team members marched past the commander's stand, performing a walking salute. Next, the Commander's wife presented service certificates and various prizes. The names of those who received certificates and prizes are omitted. A tactical demonstration was then held, first using various moving targets to demonstrate attack techniques, followed by a 200-yard machine gun shooting competition and a 300-yard small target competition. There was also a bayonet drill, using dummies as enemies to demonstrate close combat. Finally, the audience was invited into the barracks for tea and refreshments before dispersing. On that day, 136 members of the regular team were present, including Captain Wang Yanqing, Deputy Captain Wang Zhiren, and officers Hao Boyang, Yu Xianen, Yang Wenqing, and Li Yushu. In addition, a large number of reservists and veterans were also present. In total, several thousand people from all walks of life participated in the ceremony, which can be described as a grand occasion.

Engineering Society's Sightseeing Trip a Great Success

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Engineering Society, since holding a sightseeing trip a month ago, believes that sightseeing is closely related to learning, broadening horizons, and cultivating sentiments. Therefore, it was decided to visit Jiangwan and Caohejing on the 14th. On that day, two specially prepared sightseeing buses, very beautiful and comfortable, and three private cars, each displaying the society's flag, were arranged. The group departed from the society at 8:30 AM. About 40 members, both men and women, and guests attended, led by Zhu Qiqing and Zheng Baocheng. They first went to the Kang Yuan Printing and Can Manufacturing Factory. The factory is normally closed on Sundays, but the factory owner, Mr. Xiang Kangyuan, made an exception and hosted the group. The factory's scale is excellent and can be called a model factory. At the request of Mr. Xiang, Mr. Zhu Qiqing, representing the society, inscribed the four characters "Model Factory" as a memento. Next, they went to the China Experimental Chicken Farm, which has thousands of chickens of various breeds, all very beautiful and healthy. It also has a research laboratory that studies chicken-raising techniques, which is a good reference for Chinese chicken farmers and an example of the application of scientific management to small industries. The Shanghai Fuzhi Zhu Milk Company has dairy cows worth US$200,000, which can produce about 100 pounds of milk daily, which is commendable. There are also many other fine breeds. Next, they went to Tang Garden for lunch. Tang Garden is exquisitely constructed and is located about a mile west of the city center. In front of the garden is an 800-acre golf course, where many Western men and women were playing golf. Through the arrangements of the chairman, Mr. Huang Boqiao, they were able to enter and tour the garden. The lunch was specially prepared and brought along, which was very different from dining in the city. After the meal, various games were held. In the two-person three-legged race, Zhi Bingrun and Zheng Baocheng won first place. In the ball-throwing game, Xiang Kangyuan won first place. In the chopstick game, Miss Lin Nuan won first place. Her victory was not accidental, as she was quick to react. Zheng Baocheng, who won the three-legged race with Zhi Bingrun, also won first place in the one-legged race. Yang from the Foreign Affairs Office won a prize in the ball-throwing game. The winners of all the prizes were presented by Mrs. Huang Yan, with each receiving an exquisite prize. The atmosphere was filled with laughter and joy. After the games, photos were taken, and tea, refreshments, and ice cream were served. Then, they passed through the city center, where Mr. Xue Cihua, section chief of the Public Works Bureau, provided detailed guidance and explanations and distributed maps of the city center for reference. They then visited the Tianyuan Electro-Chemical Factory, which is China's first manufacturing plant that combines electricity and chemistry. The factory owner, Mr. Wu Yunzhu, is a self-made man. The equipment is very comprehensive and worthy of learning from. The Caohejing No. 1 Prison is one of the most complete model prisons, paying close attention to the health and operations of the prisoners. They returned to Shanghai in the evening, almost at dusk, nearly 7:00 PM.

This Year's Loquats are Inferior

Not Cheap and Not Beautiful

Loquats are a fruit that generates a total sales value of millions of yuan in Shanghai each year. However, due to the severe cold last winter, many of these trees have been frozen to death. Even the few that survived have produced loquats that are far inferior to those of previous years. As they are now on the market, industry insiders say that the loquats come from Dongting Mountain, Chongming, and Tangxi. This year, the goods from the east and west mountains are only enough to supply Suzhou, and even that will be insufficient. What is available in Shanghai is from Chongming and Tangxi. As a result, yesterday's market price was as high as 1.45 yuan per basket (about three catties), and even then, the supply was very limited.

Sent to the Public Security Bureau for Investigation

Fan Maojian Dies

Shang Changfa Detained for Investigation

The cooking helper Fan Maojian, 22 years old, on the boat belonging to barge owners Shen Boquan and Zhang Zhusheng, which was docked at the Wanyu Wharf on the Huangpu River in the South City, and the cooking helper Shang Changfa, only 15 years old, on Zhang's boat, were joking and jumping around on the bow of the boat at 8:00 PM last night. China Film Service Company Established

Handling Application for Inspection on Behalf of Chinese and Foreign Film Merchants

The National Government, recognizing the significant social impact of films, has ordered the Ministries of Education and Interior to send personnel to jointly form a Film Inspection Committee and has also promulgated the Film Inspection Law and its implementing regulations to supervise Chinese and foreign films. Major figures in the Shanghai film industry, noting the government's efforts to construct social psychology, fear that film merchants may not be familiar with the inspection procedures, which may cause difficulties for the Inspection Committee and make things more complicated for the film merchants. Moreover, since Nanjing and Shanghai are far apart, film merchants must send personnel to escort each film to Nanjing for inspection, which is time-consuming and costly. For foreign films, the title and description must first be translated into Chinese and submitted for approval before being returned for use during screenings. If the translator's translation is inappropriate, it may affect the film's business. Therefore, they have joined forces to organize the China Film Service Company to handle documents, descriptions, and procedures for applying for inspection of Chinese and foreign films to facilitate the implementation of the Inspection Committee and to simplify and reduce costs for film merchants. In addition to hiring talented film translators and editors, transportation experts, and experienced public servants in Shanghai, the company has also established a branch office in the capital to take responsibility for films in Nanjing and handle application matters. Preparations have been underway for several months, but the official announcement has been delayed because the Inspection Committee's orders have not been published. Now that the Ministries of Interior and Education have officially issued orders and mandated that all inspection committees established in various ports be abolished immediately, and that future submissions must be made to Nanjing, the company announces that it will officially begin operations today. Its internal organization is divided into three departments: translation and editing, transportation, and application for inspection. In addition to handling applications for inspection, the company also provides translation, description, subtitle, script, advertising, and other promotional materials for film merchants, as well as domestic and international transportation of Chinese and foreign films. The company's Shanghai head office is located at No. 112 Sichuan Road.

Nanjing Grand Theater Temporarily Closed for Renovation

The Nanjing Grand Theater in Shanghai, known for its careful consideration of decoration and the selection of films that cater to the social psychology, has attracted a large audience since its opening last spring. Yesterday, the theater suddenly announced that it would be temporarily closed starting today for renovation. It is understood that the theater's opening coincided with the end of spring, and due to weather conditions, some aspects were not as satisfactory or appropriate as desired. Moreover, the humid weather was not suitable for painting. Now that a year has passed, the architect has inspected the building and determined that it is dry and suitable for painting. Therefore, the theater is temporarily closed for renovation to improve its splendor. It is also reported that the theater's air conditioning system, which was installed at a great cost, performed well last year. Now that the weather is hot, its use is imminent. The theater also purchased soundproofing equipment from the United States to prevent noise when the machinery is running. During the renovation period, the theater will also install this equipment so that the air conditioning can be used when performances resume, providing the audience with a comfortable and hygienic temperature.

Kidnappers in Jintan Allowed to be Transferred

Qian Maoyou's seven-year-old son, a farmer from Xucun Town in Jintan County, was kidnapped on the Lantern Festival on the 30th day of the first lunar month of this year by Yao Dalai, a farmer from the same town, because his loan request was denied. Yao conspired with Wang Hongzao, Tao Sanbao, et al. from Beijing, who used weapons to kidnap Qian's son to Shanghai. They first hid the child in the homes of Zhang Changgen and a woman named Chen Tao, and then sent a letter to the victim's family demanding ransom, arranging a meeting at the North Railway Station. The incident was detected by detectives and supervisors of the French Concession Police's special agency, Jin Jiulin, Zheng Tanmu Li Yaolong, Fu Tanmu Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, Zhang Ziying, et al., who arrested Yao and the other four kidnappers and rescued the hostage in Pudong, bringing them to the police station. After questioning by the French Concession Court, they confessed to the crime and were ordered to be detained pending a letter to Jintan County, requesting them to send personnel to escort the prisoners back within a month. As reported previously, yesterday, as the deadline for the interrogation approached, a detective from Jintan County arrived to request extradition for trial. After consultation between Chinese and Western officials, the court ordered that the defendants be handed over to the detective to be taken back for trial.

Sixty-Year-Old Woman Smuggles Opium

Xu Gao, a sixty-year-old woman, purchased two large packages of opium, weighing 120 taels, and hid them on her person. She hired a rickshaw and passed through the intersection of Dagu Road and Xizang Road when she was searched by a patrol officer who discovered the opium and took her to the police station. She was sent to the Special District Local Court yesterday. After questioning by Judge Xu, she was sentenced to six months in prison and fined 100 yuan. The number of days spent in detention before the judgment was confirmed will be counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. If she is unable to pay the fine, it will be converted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan.

Dandy Cheats for Clothing

Gao Qingzhen's Empty Joy

Qi He, the son of Li Bingcheng from Guizhou Road Chengzhi, is over twenty years old and extremely frivolous, much like a dandy. His father has repeatedly disciplined him severely, but he has not repented. He was finally expelled from the family and has been wandering outside ever since. Lacking funds to spend, he resorts to swindling. There are quite a few victims. At 6:00 PM last Saturday, Qi He suddenly went to the brothel Gaogingzhen (also known as Lao Liu) at 518 Fuxiang Lane, Guangxi Road, and invited the acquainted prostitute Gaogingzhen (also known as Lao Liu) to go to Lao Jiu Lun silk and satin shop on Nanjing Road to buy clothes, promising to give the prostitute three pieces of clothing. The prostitute happily agreed and selected five or six pieces of various clothing, worth 106 yuan and 8 jiao. Qi He claimed that he did not have any cash on him and asked the shop to send a servant, Huang Jinkui, to take the clothing and go with him to get the money. When they reached the Tongyiyong Gold Shop at the intersection of Jiujiang Road and Xizang Road, Qi He ordered Huang to wait temporarily while he took the items upstairs. He then came downstairs and said to Huang that the price was too high and asked him to call the shop to inquire whether they could offer a discount. Huang went to find a telephone, and by the time he was done, both Qi He and Gaogingzhen had disappeared, and the clothing had also been taken. Realizing that he had been cheated, he quickly returned to the shop to report to the manager, who reported it to the Lao Zha Police Station. Detectives were dispatched to Gaogingzhen's residence to inquire, but she did not know Qi He's whereabouts either. The next evening, Gaogingzhen received a phone call and learned that he was hiding in Room 150 of the Andong Hotel on Hubei Road. Detectives went with her to arrest him and seized the stolen goods. He was sent to the Special District Local Court for questioning yesterday. The defendant admitted to the crime without hesitation. The police lawyer Qian Xunjiu said that he had committed many crimes and still needed to be investigated, requesting a postponement. The court ordered the defendant to be detained pending interrogation.

Enquina Obtains Trademark Rights for Cigars

"Old Beauty" and "Comet"

The "Old Beauty" and "Comet" cigars exclusively issued by the Belgian company Enquina were confiscated and auctioned by the US government to the Olsen Company in Little Luzon during World War I because they were suspected of being French. The US cigar manufacturer then issued the cigars in various parts of China. After the end of World War I, the auction price was returned, but because the position of the Olsen Company was unaffected, a dispute arose over the issue of trademark exclusivity. The Trademark Bureau re-evaluated the case, and the Ministry of Industry recently made a final decision that all "Old Beauty" and "Comet" trademarks belong exclusively to Enquina. The registration certificate of the US Cigar Company has also been formally revoked.

Letter to the Editor

Labor's Reply to the Guanghua Factory's Letter: Having read the Guanghua Factory's letter attached to the report of the Guanghua Factory labor dispute yesterday in Shen Bao, we were deeply shocked. Upon investigation, the contents of the letter are not only completely unfounded but also simply fabricated facts, confusing the public. In order to clarify the situation of the oppressed workers to the outside world, we make the following painful and sincere rebuttal:

Guanghua Factory has been in operation for ten years. Before He Guyongquan joined the factory, there was never any announcement from the factory about annual losses or intentions to cease operations. He Guyongquan used to be the person in charge of silk weaving, responsible for leading and training workers, without a doubt. If workers were not working hard enough for the factory, they should have been sincerely persuaded to improve. How could it be that only after acquiring the position of factory manager did he claim that the factory was losing money because the workers were not working hard enough? Moreover, He Guyongquan is an uneducated person. Whether he has any experience in factory management is obvious. The factory bought and sold the workers' labor, destroyed the labor union, strictly enforced factory regulations, signed short-term employment contracts, and oppressed the workers. Since He Yongquan entered the factory this February 15, he has recorded hundreds of large and small infractions, dismissing more than seventy workers. What others are unwilling, unable, or dare not to do, he has done, setting a new record for factory managers using tyrannical power. The cause of this labor dispute was that worker Zhu Linhou accidentally splashed medicine on his body while working, fearing that his clothes would be ruined and his skin burned. It seems reasonable to take off his clothes to wash them and there was no reason to dismiss him. After repeated negotiations by the labor union, the factory had agreed to reinstate him. However, He Guyongquan, regardless of the workers' livelihood, obstructs reinstatement, requiring the worker to write a letter of repentance and the labor union to provide a letter of guarantee, stating that if any further incidents occur, large or small, the worker will be immediately dismissed, and the labor union will not be allowed to inquire. This kind of coercion cuts off the workers' lifeline. However, in order to take into account labor-management cooperation and factory management, the labor union prepared a letter to the factory stating that the worker had been reprimanded and would not be allowed to cause similar incidents in the future. The labor union also severely warned the worker before he was reinstated. However, He Guyongquan, on the pretext that the labor union's letter did not meet his requirements, returned the letter and on June 8, again expelled Zhu Linhou from the factory, publicly humiliating him. It is undeniable that He Guyongquan has falsely accused all the workers of assaulting him, causing him injuries, and claiming that the workers broke into his office, overturned tables and chairs, and smashed bowls and plates. As for the issue of workers living in the factory, it was originally the factory's decision to stop supplying raw materials, causing panic among the workers about their livelihood, and the proposal to live in the factory was decided by the entire worker's conference. It was definitely not something that Liu Jintai could dictate. Now the factory is attacking Liu Jintai personally and using this fabricated accusation to alienate loyal comrades in the labor union. When the factory saw that the workers were united and there was no way to take advantage, it demanded that the labor union leaders discuss a solution. Therefore, the labor union accepted the demands of all the workers and discussed a solution together. At that time, police officers Wang Sheng and Er from the Fifth Precinct of the Second District Public Security Bureau mediated nearby. However, the workers believed that Officer Wang was responsible for public security and could not overstep his authority to mediate a labor-management dispute that was unrelated to public security. As for how they were coerced into signing, how they surrounded the general manager, and how they beat Officer Wang, causing him serious injuries, all of these are completely contrary to the facts. Moreover, after the labor dispute occurred, the labor union immediately reported to the competent authorities for handling, and the workers were quiet as usual. However, the factory fabricated rumors and blamed the workers. Even worse, it openly claimed that Officer Wang was beaten, which is an insult to public officials. Now, our association refutes the factory's fabricated facts, recounts the course of the labor dispute, and describes He Guyongquan's oppression of the workers as above. We hope that people in society will understand the truth. Wang Wenhua of the Publishing Industry Labor Union, Lu Muqin of the Pharmaceutical Industry Labor Union.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom

— Yi Mei

Indifference is the suitable continuation of divinity. It is often destroyed by material civilization.

The fire of desire cannot be indulged, for it will consume oneself. The tide of emotion cannot be breached, for it will drown oneself.

Multiple and complicated taxes cannot be levied on mirages in the marketplace.

Sleep is temporary death; death is permanent sleep.

A heartbroken person has special feelings; a wise person has their own unique insight.

There are famous generals who are vigorous in old age, but no beautiful women who become more beautiful with age.

There are many smiles in the city, but nine out of ten are feigned.

My birthday is the anniversary of my mother's departure, so rather than celebrating with wine and merriment, it is better to devote myself to filial piety and provide for her every need.

No raft in the sea of consciousness; no grain in the fields of the heart.

To understand people is to be able to navigate the world; to preserve one's own simplicity is to be able to conduct oneself with integrity.

Flowers are the passionate lovers of butterflies; butterflies are the unfaithful lads of flowers.

Famous flowers are destroyed by wind and rain; good books are eaten by bookworms; bright moons are obscured by clouds and mist; youth is damaged by sensual pleasures. These are the four great regrets of the universe.

It is easy to wash away dirt; it is difficult to cleanse shame.

Those wounded by the arrows of love often die without treatment.

Trivial Notes on Commander Xiong's Banquet for Fundraising

— Sun Choucheng

Commander Xiong Tianyi, in order to solicit donations for the Jiangxi disaster relief, made a special trip back to Shanghai before accompanying Chairman Chiang to Jiangxi to suppress the communists. On the evening of the 13th, he hosted a banquet at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to entertain leaders from various industries. The general situation has already been reported in the newspapers the next day. Here, I supplement the details that were not reported by various newspapers.

The public banquet was originally scheduled for 6 PM. I arrived on time. A registration desk was set up next to the stone steps, with Doctor Wang Peiyuan, Secretary Shu Ruifeng, and various staff members from the Red Cross Society Songhu Garrison Headquarters warmly greeting guests to the third floor for refreshments. There were three areas: the Standing Committee Room, the Reception Hall, and the veranda. The weather was unusually hot that day, and the veranda was cooler, so everyone went there. After Commander Xiong arrived, he discussed with Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jingren, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others in the reception room on the second floor about asking famous Peking opera actors in Shanghai to perform charity shows for a few days to raise relief funds. Shortly after, they entered the banquet hall. The banquet was set up in the Grand Hall, divided into five rows, with five tables in each row, all round tables. The food was provided by Jue Lin Vegetarian Restaurant. When Commander Xiong led the guests into the hall, he was all smiles and frequently nodded in greeting. Du Yuesheng took this opportunity to shake hands with the guests and expressed his apologies for the inadequate hospitality due to the large number of guests attending the completion of his family temple. The table in the center, closest to the north, was the head table. Commander Xiong invited Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, and others to sit at this table. Shi Liangcai, Huang Hanzhi, Wu Yunzhai, Wen Lanting, Lin Kanghou, Zheng Chengqing, Wu Zhihao, Lu Qisheng, and others sat at the second table. First, a large basin of steamed buns was served. After the guests ate, Xu Shiying tapped his cup with his chopsticks, and Wang Xiaolai clapped in agreement. Commander Xiong then stood up to report on the Jiangxi disaster situation. This is a pandemic like influenza. If it is not rescued, it may spread to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and then to the entire country. His words were very sincere, and the listeners were moved. Zhang Xiaolin, after hearing Commander Xiong's report that bandits in Jiangxi would kill anyone over thirty years old, those with more than five hundred yuan in property, and those in the intelligentsia, could not help but blurt out that everyone present tonight was qualified to be killed. Everyone gasped. Xu Shiying said that because he was the chairman of the Relief Committee, he had more accurate information about the Jiangxi disaster. Everyone was already saddened to tears after watching the film about the Shaanxi disaster. Little did they know that the Jiangxi disaster was even more severe than the Shaanxi disaster. In one case, there were still people going to investigate the disaster and find ways to provide relief. In the other, people were afraid of being harmed by the communists, and no one dared to pay to bury the exposed corpses and the dying people. Seventy-three counties were desolate everywhere, with no signs of human habitation for dozens of miles. It was too terrible to bear. Donating one yuan could save a life. Saving people is saving oneself. There will be unseen rewards. Yu Qiaqing said that Shanghai has recently been paying attention to and worried about the situation in Guangdong. What people don't know is that Guangdong is not a problem. Jiangxi is a neighboring province to Jiangsu and Zhejiang. If there is no solution, the harm will be far greater than in Guangdong. Please give generously to help. Wen Lanting proposed that those who attended the meeting become fundraising committee members. Then Wu Zhihao, Zheng Chengqing, and others divided into teams, holding donation books and account books, and personally distributed them to each table. Everyone was given a small booklet "A Glimpse of the Jiangxi Disaster," which contained many photos of the destruction caused by the bandits. Many people made donations on the spot, with Zhou Xiangyun and Zhou Chunqing jointly donating five thousand yuan, the largest amount. The banquet ended at 9 PM. I record it with a pen.

Ballad of the Huai River

— Zhuang Songfu

Written during an inspection tour of the Huai River in June of the 20th year of the Republic of China, leaving a lasting impression.

The Yangtze is long, the Yellow River is yellow. The Huai River is in the center. From Tongbai in the west to the East China Sea in the east. Mountain torrents erupt, a vast ocean. Drought demons descend, famine everywhere. The old and weak are in the ditches, the strong flee in all directions. Who will devote their efforts to the ditches and canals, so that crops will be abundant and the people prosperous?

Reflections

— Cao Mengyu

The Xiang River has dried up, and tear stains have vanished. Only her beautiful image remains on the wall. Having weathered the storms of the sea of love, the next eighteen stages are still a dangerous shoal.

I know that melancholy is pointless. But it is easy to be enchanted by her clear beauty. I resent the old man under the moon, who ties too many uneven red threads.

Talking About Wax Beauties

— Qingmen Hermit

A wax-made beauty head is a kind of artwork. The maker must have a full aesthetic concept of the human body's skeletal and muscular structure, and have the ability to carve and paint with ease, only then can they be competent. The matching of materials also requires a thorough understanding of physics and chemistry. First, the finished product must not be heated and melted in sunlight or under electric lights, so its melting point must be at least 100 degrees Fahrenheit. Second, the skin color must be as clear as jade, without any oiliness, spots, or blemishes. This point is the most difficult to grasp, because at the time of its birth, it is only roughly modeled, with slight concavities and convexities. It all depends on the knife to cut and shape it to get its appearance. If there are any changes in the cold, warmth, dryness, and humidity of the weather, then its solidification point will be different. Often, it is like alum stone, with the inside and outside having different levels of fineness, unable to be consistent throughout. If flaws are discovered, there is absolutely no way to remedy them, and the work of repairing and shaping is therefore limited. Therefore, those made in Europe and America are priced from hundreds of American dollars to five or six hundred dollars. Generally, they are divided into five grades. The ordinary ones are made of paper and powdered, and the eyebrows and eyes are all painted, worth eighty US dollars. The wax ones are equipped with eyebrows and eyes, but the eyelashes are still painted, and the eyeballs are also made of wax, but the pupils are made of convex glass. The price is already twice as high as the ordinary ones. Most of them have scars on their faces and cannot be looked at closely. They are likened to pheasants under electric lights, which can be said to be an excellent critique. If the skin color is clear, clean, beautiful, and like a person in a painting, then its value is always between three and four times higher. If it looks like alum stone and is fitted with a medical prosthetic eye, it is actually worth 600 US dollars, equivalent to more than 2,000 taels of silver, which is also amazing. The cheapest is the Eastern-style ancient painting beauty, the whole body is only twenty yuan. In the past, only Sang Dongchen was a master of making Chinese ones. Unfortunately, the raw materials he used were not wax, so the eyebrows and eyes were like paintings. Although they were charming, the skin color always felt lifeless. I once sighed that it was perfect but not perfect, and I didn't understand why wax couldn't be used. Only now do I know that wax-making cannot be relied upon, as there are the various difficulties mentioned above, because it is not as self-directed as clay sculpture and paper pasting. However, the clay sculpted heads of Huishan are also worth more than thirty yuan. The heads made by the Buddha statue workshops in the area of the New North Gate are also not cheap. The first shortcoming is that they look like dead faces of clay sculpture and wood carving. I once asked copper statue sculptors why they don't make this. I didn't know that the value of a copper statue is at least four or five thousand gold. The same amount of work is required, so they don't bother with these trivial things. It's no wonder. I often regret that I have never learned to paint, and I can only make wax fruits, but I can't make wax beauty heads. I have been looking for a partner for several years, but I have not been able to find one. Yesterday, I accidentally visited Tian Xuwo at Xiangxuelou, and he was using a knife to make a wax beauty head on a rotating frame. I laughed in surprise, and after inquiring in detail, I learned that it was made by his younger brother Rongxuan. It was shipped from Wuxi to Shanghai and had been damaged, so he was changing it into a thinner face, and the skin was turning clear. The person was like jade, truly perfect. Asking about the price, it was only sixty yuan to one hundred and twenty yuan. The difference in price also depended on the solidification state of the wax. If it was fitted with a full body, then half the price would be added. I praised it endlessly and asked for permission to take a photo as a groundbreaking memorial.

After the photo was taken, everyone who saw it mistook it for the real thing, which shows how skillful it is. There are two photos in total. The first is of Rongxuan's original work, and the second is of Tian Xuwo's modified work. They are displayed at the National Products Mall in the New World and look exactly like twin sisters, with only the difference between the plump Huan and the slender Yan. Some say that Rongxuan's work looks exactly like Xiao Yang Yuelou, and the curly hair is like clouds, all having been electrically ironed, which was made by Miss Xiao Cui.

Publishing News: "Commercial Monthly", edited by Mr. Shi Bohang, professor of National Jiji University, Daxia University, Central University School of Commerce, etc., has now been published for its "Inaugural Issue". The content is rich. There are thirteen articles by Mr. Ma Yinchu, Wang Danru, Liu Zhonglian, etc. In particular, the classified index of major commercial events in the daily newspapers of the past month is a special feature. It is reported that the publication is distributed by Shanghai Ximenwai Anhulu Ruiqingli Commercial Abacus Society. The price is two corners per copy, and the annual subscription is two yuan, three yuan for overseas. There is also a gift.

Photographs of the Du Ancestral Hall Gathering

— Qian Hua

The completion ceremony of Mr. Du Yuesheng's ancestral hall in Gaoqiao, Pudong, was celebrated with a grand three-day gathering from June 9th to 11th. Famous performers from both the north and south were invited, including the four great female impersonators, Mei Lanfang, Shang Xiaoyun, Cheng Yanqiu, and Xun Huisheng, as well as Yang Xiaolou, Xi Yunfu, Wang Youchen, Ma Lianliang, Tan Xiaopei and his son, Wang Shaolou, Gao Qingkui, Yan Jupeng, and others, all participating. It can be said to be an unprecedented gathering in Shanghai. The number of guests reached tens of thousands each day. The road to Gaoqiao was filled with a cloud of carriages.

The Glamour of Small Cars　From the Gaoqiao ferry to the Du Ancestral Hall is still a distance of ten li. The community residence prepared dozens of cars and one hundred and fifty rickshaws to pick up and drop off guests, but it was a drop in the bucket and did not solve the problem. Most people still walked back and forth. Those who managed to intercept a few rickshaws along the way were seen as being blessed by good fortune. Although the price was exorbitant, ranging from one to three or four yuan for a one-way trip, people were happy to pay. The countryside's wheelbarrows were therefore in great demand and could not keep up. A one-way trip also cost one yuan. Modernly dressed women sitting on them added a unique scene. Many said it was their first time trying it.

White-Hot Popularity　The theater could accommodate several thousand people, but there were nearly ten thousand spectators, leaving almost no room to stand. Coupled with the hot weather and the low-lying terrain, the surroundings were airtight. Spectators waved their fans while watching the play, and everyone was drenched in sweat. The air in the entire theater was extremely turbid. The phrase "white-hot popularity" is the most appropriate description. Zhang Xiaolin and Wang Xiaolai maintained order, but even they could not disperse the spectators on stage. In the evening, guests continued to arrive one after another. Thousands of people who had traveled more than ten li retreated due to the difficulty. Those who had secured a place in the VIP seats, although enjoying the pleasure of sight and sound, sat through the night, breathing rapidly, with splitting headaches, unable to move their bodies. They were in a situation where they wanted to stop but could not. It was truly an unspeakable pain.

Most Splendid　Among the three-day program, the second day (i.e., the 10th) was the most splendid. The performances included Li Jirui's "Dumu Pass," Little Guiyuan's "Drumming and Scolding Cao," Xu Biyun's "Hua Mulan," Li Wanchun and Lan Yuechun's "The Two Generals," Cheng Yanqiu's "Guan Dayuan Scolding the Palace," Liu Zongyang's "An Tianhui," Wang Shaogen and Hua Huilin's "Sitting in the Palace," Wang Youchen's "Selling the Horse," and Yang Xiaolou and Xue Yanqin's "Changban Slope." The final performance was the complete "Red Mane Stallion" by Mei Lanfang, Shang Xiaoyun, Xun Huisheng, and Xue Yanqin and Ma Lianliang. The arrangement was neat and tidy, a sight to behold.

Brief Reviews of Each Play　Cheng Yanqiu's "Scolding the Palace" has long been famous. That evening, he performed with even more effort. His singing voice was melodious, with ups and downs, winning rounds of applause. Liu Zongyang, the only beloved disciple of Cha Xiaolou, played "An Tianhui," and he did resemble him in some ways. Wang Shaolou's "Sitting in the Palace" featured several major singing sections, all reaching the highest level. The *yuanban* segment of "Flowing Water and the Virtuous Princess" was particularly good. Wang Youchen's "Selling the Horse" was one of the most popular plays that evening. Wang's expression and demeanor closely resembled the late Jiao Tian. His voice was clear and sweet, and his enunciation was solid. The "Innkeeper" segment was met with applause for every line. It was truly a work of pure mastery, transcending the ordinary. Yang Xiaolou's "Changban Slope" is famous among women and children. Paired with Gao Qingkui's Liu Bei, Xue Yanqin's Lady Mi, and Liu Yanting's Zhang Fei, it added to the luster. However, the grabbing of the *pei* in one scene was not clean enough, a minor flaw in an otherwise perfect performance. Finally, the complete "Red Mane Stallion" featured Xu Biyun first singing "Choosing a Mate from the Embroidered Tower," followed by Shang Xiaoyun's "Three Slaps on the Table," Qilin Tong Wang Yunfang's "Leaving the Kiln," Guo Zhongheng and Rongcao's "Chasing the Three Passes," Mei Lanfang, Tan Fuying, and Yan Jupeng singing "Wujiapo" together, Tan Xiaopei and Xue Yanqin's "Calculating the Grain," and Tan Xiaopei, Xun Huisheng, and Jiang Miaoxiang's "Silver Empty Mountain." The finale was Mei Lanfang, Xun Huisheng, Xi Yunfu, and Ma Lianliang's "Grand Ascension to the Throne." The arrangement of this play was neat and tidy, bringing together the four great female impersonators in one performance. From beginning to end, the spirit was consistent. It can not only be described as unprecedented, but also as unparalleled.

Rotary Club Storytelling

Three Eras (7)

— Zhang Henshui

(3) The Orator of Tianqiao

Zhang Xiaosan'er no longer had his family. Not only did he not feel lonely, but he felt free. Besides his own eating and drinking, he didn't have to worry about anything at home. One day, he pulled two fares and had some money. He didn't run anymore. He turned in his rickshaw early and went to Tianqiao to hang out. Tianqiao was an enlarged department store and playground for the lower classes. It could be said that it had everything one could want. Everywhere were broken reed mat sheds, everywhere was the smell of urine and feces. Naturally, many people were intoxicated there. Zhang Xiaosan'er was also a Tianqiao enthusiast, especially fond of Xiao Ma Wu's Hua Dan in the Bangzi opera. He admired him twenty-four-fold. As soon as he arrived at Tianqiao, he found out that Xiao Ma Wu was singing "Spinning Cotton" today. Excellent! He rushed to the entrance of the reed mat shed stage, but the people inside were surging outwards, saying that there was no room to stand. He squeezed in to take a look. Indeed, there wasn't. He walked out dejectedly, not knowing where to go. He walked aimlessly. He squeezed into the crowds watching Yunli Fei's comic dialogue and the one-man bear performance. Accidentally crossing the street, he saw a small white flag fluttering above the crowd. There was a cluster of people surrounding the flag. Zhang Xiaosan'er thought, maybe it's some new gimmick. Let's go forward and take a look. He squeezed into the crowd and saw two soldiers in gray uniforms standing in the middle. One was holding the flag, and the other had both arms raised, standing there speaking. While he was speaking, many people laughed along with him. Behind the two of them was a large beggar, the one he always saw begging on the street. The other two people were a fifteen or sixteen-year-old child and a forty or fifty-year-old man. Just looking at the white coats they were wearing, without the two half sleeves, and dyed gray-black, they were definitely rickshaw pullers. Those few people were lowering their heads and not saying a word, not as happy as the others listening. The speaking soldier was very unreserved. He gestured while speaking. Seeing Zhang Xiaosan'er come in, he glanced at him and said with a smile, "Here comes another one. I bet he has nothing to do either. You don't have to say that people who have nothing to do, even if they do, are not as happy as being a soldier. After two exercises and three classes a day, we just sleep. Making a living and selling labor all have to worry about where today's meal money will come from. Soldiers don't have to worry about that. We eat when we hear the bugle. We don't buy tickets when we take the streetcar. We don't buy tickets when we take the train. We go wherever we want. If we're not wearing our uniforms, sneaking into the theater to listen to free opera is so embarrassing. When we're wearing our uniforms, we have priority seating. We've seen all the famous actors after listening to opera for a few years, but we haven't spent a single cent. Speaking of going to brothels, haha..."

Commercial News

Financial Gold Price Strongly Rebounds

Letting Go of Swap, Cashing In

Soars Ten Taels and Three Mace

Almost Reaching Its Peak　Yesterday, the 15th, the gold auction rose sharply again, once breaking through the 80 tael mark. The momentum of the rise was truly unexpected, proceeding quickly. The opening was only two or three taels, but the overall market was fourteen or fifteen taels. In the end, it soared by ten taels and some, almost reaching its peak, above 810 taels. However, the exchange rate was slightly higher, so the final price was between 808 taels. The industry had privately opened swaps in advance, initially with the bulls posting a premium of two taels, but there were few transactions. Subsequently, they calculated 1.2 mace to 4.5 mace. Then, the Dalian gang, who were bears, posted a premium of 1.1 to 1.2 mace (these were swapped out by Daxingyong and other bulls). Subsequently, Hengxing (doing the opposite swap), which was originally a bull, deliberately swapped to become a bear, thus posting a premium of one tael. Then it was leveled off, with a total transaction of more than 10,000 contracts. This approach was profitable, so to speak, clever and quick-witted. However, the bears had suffered an infinite impact, thus the July market price has been aroused. Afterwards, the bears were posting a premium of about one tael, which was bewildering. Perhaps there will be some changes in today's (16th) official swap.

No Special Changes in the Early Morning　The July opening slightly increased by 7 mace to 798.5 taels. However, because the big contracts only increased by 1/16 and the silver price did not change, people were unmoved. Subsequently, Yuancheng, Yongyi, Yu, and Wupin sold, which suppressed it to 96.1 taels. Then Yuanchun and Hengyu bought in, so it rose by two taels to 8.2 to 3 mace. The Xianling announcement remained unchanged, at 7.7 mace. Subsequently, the downstream went up by one tael. Due to the sale by Yuanmaoyong and others, it was 96.3 to 4 taels at 10 o'clock. Afterwards, Sumitomo absorbed British March 3125, and various companies slightly purchased, so it increased by more than one tael. However, the market situation was flat, without excessive prosperity or disgrace. Until 11 o'clock, a wave suddenly rose. It was heard that the large bull accounts were unwilling to swap the period, intending to collect cash. All of a sudden, the bears were horrified, and they followed and entered, killing them and scattering them. The price shot up with a burst, suddenly breaking through 800 taels. Customer Sales of 6,025 Bales

The actual demand for cotton yarn is becoming more smooth. The Sichuan gang is purchasing very enthusiastically, and mostly buying local yarn. Therefore, the market price is increasing daily. The political situation news is good, and the gold price is surging again, which strengthens people's confidence. Therefore, the later market can rise. However, most sellers think that the overseas situation is still calm and the sales of coarse yarn are still sluggish, so they are mentally weak and have no intention of buying empty. Therefore, although the current yarn sales are strong, the marked yarn cannot have a great increase in strength. However, if the current sales continue, there will be a great change in the future.

Yarn Sales Are Very Lively　Current yarn sales are still developing. It was found that each gang bought a total of 6,025 bales of spot and future goods throughout the day, and the prices rose 5 qian to 1-2 taels. Among the customer gangs, Sichuan entered 1,955 bales, Hankou entered 100 bales, Guangdong entered 200 bales, and futures 1,500 bales, Shantou entered 200 bales, the North gang entered 150 bales, Yunnan entered 350 bales, Ningbo entered 75 bales, the Mainland entered 300 bales, Tianjin entered 80 bales, and miscellaneous gangs entered 150 bales.

Cotton Market Calm

The cotton market was calm, tired in the morning and rising in the afternoon. However, the overseas cotton market was still soft, and people's hearts were not excited. In the afternoon, the gold price surged again, and the yarn market was also good at the same time, so it slightly brought up some rises. However, the market situation was extremely calm, and there was nothing very exciting to say.

Han Mark Slightly Up and Down　The Han Mark front market did not do well with overseas cotton, falling by 5 points to 1 qian. It rose slightly by 1 qian and 5 points in the afternoon. The total daily transaction was 18,100 dans. It was found that Gongtai sold 900 dans and Shenji sold 700 dans. Shenda bought 700 dans, Tianlong bought 700 dans, and Zhenda bought 500 dans. Weekly British Indian Cotton Industry Report

Bombay: Last week, market prices fluctuated with U.S. cotton. While New York market prices showed smaller changes, the hedging variations in Bombay were also small. There were no signs of weakness in the Bombay market. The statistical situation remains solid, with strong current demand. Local factories have purchased a considerable amount of mixed cotton. Transactions by European exporters were quiet. Japanese merchants purchased Oomras and Khandesh cotton in substantial quantities. A significant amount of Oomras and Bengal cotton were shipped to Shanghai. The following is a summary of last week's statistics (in thousands of bales):

Liverpool: Spot transactions were more active last week. In terms of futures, market sentiment gradually improved after new low prices were seen. Market price fluctuations were small, and the weekend was particularly firm. Egyptian cotton moved in response to overseas markets, gradually improving over the weekend following U.S. cotton news.

Grains: Dujian rice is the firmest, while thick japonica rice is stable.

Zhabei: Yesterday, the rice market was still not fully active due to the slack market conditions in the interior. However, there are still many stocks in the city, making it difficult for the river market to rally. The number of people visiting the market in the morning was still low, mostly inquiring about news. It was difficult to increase sales. Changshu and Northern Japonica rice remained stable, and mid-grade goods moved slightly, so prices rose by one "chi." Thin and early rice still showed no signs of stabilizing. Dujian rice sales were more active, so prices were tight. Lower grades of Yangpu Jian rice showed weakness. Glutinous rice saw no special fluctuations, and Yin Hua rice was also stable. Purchases of Ke Jian rice by local merchants were still weak, and prices remained firm.

South Shanghai: Yesterday, the market sentiment was very good, and the number of visitors to the market was still strong. River transport was acceptable due to the rainy weather and the gradual scarcity of arrivals. It was also heard that the northern market was becoming more active, and market sentiment was trending upwards, suddenly increasing prices. Sales were also thin. With the busy farming season, transportation from production areas was difficult, and market prices suddenly increased. High-quality thick Japonica rice rose by two jiao. Arrivals of thin rice were slightly scarce, but there were about twenty to thirty "hao" of accumulated goods in the river. Ningbo sales were scattered, and local merchants were only picking out the freshest high-quality rice. Mid-grade qualities were still limited, resulting in a price increase of over a jiao. Arrivals and sales of foreign Dujian rice were even, with no market gains or losses. The daily demand for Yin Hua rice was not weak, and the market situation was also tight by perhaps a jiao.

Distant Month Flour Slightly Down

Yesterday's flour market: After the market opened in the morning, various months initially saw firming market sentiment due to foreign wheat quotations rising by about one or two jiao, appearing slightly better than the previous weekend's closing. However, later, as the sentiment of inland buyers turned weak, sellers gradually became more prevalent, and market sentiment again stepped downwards. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, market sentiment was even more depressed. Although factory sales were not launched on a large scale, the wheat harvest was good, and actual sales in the north were not very active. Because average daily sales in Tianjin were only twenty to thirty thousand bags, about two-thirds less than the peak sales volume, the current weakness is quite in line with the facts. As a result, this month saw no change, while July through November each fell by 1.25 fen.

Futures Wheat Market Hovering

Yesterday's futures wheat market: After the market opened in the morning and afternoon, various months generally showed a hovering pattern. Because foreign wheat quotations were slightly better, sentiment towards the middle was inevitably stabilized. Moreover, although the new wheat had already entered the market, arrivals were not very strong. Therefore, although the situation had a tendency to decline, the bulls remained stubbornly resisting. Given this state, if the stubborn resistance is excessive, the standard for the future may shift to a sale of more spot goods. At that time, with matched strength, there will surely be a distinction between strong and weak. As a result, this month was up two fen from the previous week, July was unchanged, August was up one fen, September was unchanged, October was down two fen, and November was down one fen. In the spot wheat market, arrivals were more abundant. Since factories still have foreign wheat, they generally take a non-discounted approach to buying. Nanjing wheat opened at 3 liang, 8 qian, and 7 fen; Hezhou wheat opened at 3 liang, 8 qian, and 2 fen; lower grades were at 3 liang, 2 qian, and 7 fen, with a total of 8,404 bags, handled by Fuxin.

Fuzhou Traders Procure Ke Xian Rice

Yesterday's Ke Xian rice market: Although prices did not rise, sales were slightly active. After a pause in the local market, Fuzhou traders suddenly started trying to procure. The night before last, more than 300 bags of Jiangxi Ji Wan rice were procured, priced at 11 yuan and 5 fen to 10 yuan. Yesterday afternoon, another 230 bags were procured, priced at 10 yuan and 8 or 9 jiao. The goods were all ordinary goods from the general market. Although some hoarders purchased high-quality goods and stored them, they were unwilling to lightly sell due to the small margins. There was no change in imports and exports of foreign rice, and no reverse sales were made. This was because the market was very weak, importers were watching, and cargo owners were unwilling to lower prices for sales due to high costs.

Silk and Tea: Jiangbei Spring Cocoons' Silk Reeling Yields Exceptionally Low

Foreign variety cocoons require over 600 jin... Local variety cocoons require around 800 jin. In Taixian, Taixing, Rugao, Huaiyin, and other areas of Jiangbei, this year's spring silkworms have suffered greatly from the weather. Cocoon production is exceptionally low, amounting to less than three-tenths of a normal year. Due to excessive rain and cold, the cocoons did not produce enough silk, with many thin-skinned and double cocoons. Newly-styled cocoons have been tested for reeling, requiring 340 to 350 jin for baking and threshing. The lowest yield is for local cocoons, requiring around 800 jin (dry cocoons) to reel 100 jin of silk. Foreign variety cocoons also require 620 to 630 jin.

Yellow Silk Thread Difficult to Improve Sales

Yesterday's Shanghai foreign-owned silk market still showed no improvement. European and American markets and raw silk factory sales are still slow. Telegrams for white silk thread did not improve yesterday, and yellow silk thread from British and Indian companies also found it difficult to increase sales due to high prices. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson and others imported only 25 bales of yellow factory silk, while Meida and others imported 40 bales of yellow coarse silk, with prices remaining stable.

Lu Zhuang's Zhen Mei Tea Sales in Europe Depressed

Yesterday, the green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi and other areas of Lu Zhuang, with various tea shops putting out no less than two thousand boxes of new styles. There were some scattered transactions for needle tea and Gong Xi teas. Most importantly, for Zhen Mei green tea, except for a few purchases of core-extracted goods by the British company Jardine Matheson, everyone else remained in a wait-and-see attitude. The reason for this is that France still has abundant tea stocks and does not urgently need new goods. The opening prices for Tunxi and Wuyuan Zhen Mei tea last week were too high, causing overseas tea merchants to shy away. However, Chinese merchants were trending towards stability because harvests from various regions were 50% less than last year. Therefore, the whole market did not open for ordinary Zhen Mei tea.

North-South Goods: Hunan Lotus Seed Sources Have Been Exhausted

Recently, Hunan lotus seeds have been in exceptionally firm market conditions because of the lack of inventory in production areas. Current prices are as follows: Top-grade Xiangtan lotus seeds sell for 37 to 38 liang, followed by 35 to 36 liang. Changde lotus seeds sell for 33 to 34 liang. Guangdong traders occasionally make purchases, but in small quantities. It is reported that since local goods have been exhausted, the market will be good in the future. Therefore, most people have agreed not to sell cheaply, and further price increases are likely in the future.

Metals: British Steel Plates Being Hoarded

Transactions of British steel plates have recently made good progress, with Tianjin, Qingdao, Yantai, and other traders having a few transactions every day, so transactions amount to 600 or 700 dan. However, base goods are not thick. Hoarders, seeing the scarcity of sources and the high set prices, have thoughts of hoarding. An investigation found that 2,000 or 3,000 dan have been purchased, and the prices have been driven up quite a bit. Current market prices are: 2.5 li selling for 9 liang, 8 fen; 7 li selling for 7 liang, 2 qian, 5 fen; 7.5 li selling for 7 liang; 1 fen selling for 6 liang, 5 qian.

Sugar Market: Coarse Sand White Sugar Gradually Trending Upwards

Yesterday, there were no dispatches from the sugar production areas. The public market was divided outside the market due to higher foreign exchange rates, and sentiment was slightly tight. The transaction price of Dutch No. 24 ordinary coarse sand white sugar and Hong Kong goods was 11 liang, 6 qian, and sellers were not many. High-quality goods were priced at 11 liang, 7 qian, but few inquired. No. 20 medium sand white sugar was at 10 liang and 9 qian, 5 fen, and transactions were also few. The Japanese sugar market also rose slightly, but the trend was relatively flat. Z lai was at 11 liang, 3 qian, 2 fen, 5 li, and TK was at the same price, all old goods. Newly arrived goods were priced at 11 liang, 4 qian, YT was at 11 liang, 3 qian, 5 fen, YRO was at 11 liang, YP was at 11 liang, 7 qian, 1 fen, 2.5 li, AE was at 11 liang, 7 qian, SH was at 11 liang, 1 qian, and TM was at 11 liang, 2 qian, 2 fen, 5 li. The market was still bullish. Hao Pan Zhen Xiang Hao opened with 2,000 bags of spot Hong Kong coarse sand white sugar, priced at 11 liang, 6 qian. Yu Fa and Zhang Tai No. 2 opened with several hundred bags of local factory Binghua Qing, both priced at 10 liang. The original goods opened at 10 liang and 3 qian, and the market was firm. For sellers of Dutch red sugar, No. 8 and 9 goods, Jiecheng foreign company was quite accommodating, priced at 4 yuan and 9 jiao, 5 fen in Dutch currency, and buyers were very few.

Piece Goods: Rising Piece Goods

Local Cotton Cloth: Yesterday's market was increasingly firm, with fine cloth in great demand. Blue Chicken has reached 7 liang, 5 qian, and some fen. Yang He Cao Ba Zhang Lan Double Fish all rose by 5 fen. Fine twill Blue Double Fish was suddenly needed by Sichuan traders, with more than 300 pieces transacted, so it suddenly rose by 1 qian. Spot goods of 9-pound coarse cloth are still scarce, and 11-pound cloth is also firm. The sales of Hubei Tianzi Yi Feng have ceased. Yesterday, it sold for 8 liang, 8 qian. Jin San Ta bleached cloth continued to rise to 9 liang, 4 qian. Sales of coarse remnant thread are still slow, so there is no major change. 84 original cloth also rose, with Blue Flying Fish at 6 liang and 1 qian, 5 fen, and Lu Wu at 6 liang and 1 qian.

Eastern and Western Piece Goods: All rose sharply, especially Eastern goods. Yesterday, fine yarn rose by 2.5 li. Top-quality Zhigong satin is gradually becoming scarce. Mid-range Sanyou patterns sold out at 3 qian and 5 fen. Six Scholars opened at 3 qian and 6 fen, 5 li, and First Merit at 3 qian and 7 fen, 5 li. Striped Fu Chou rose again after falling, and miscellaneous colors are out of stock. Tu Bai Huxin Ting and Yang Guifei are all at 3 qian and 8 fen. Snowflake yarn, after being procured by Tianjin traders, has gradually become brisk. Yesterday, spot goods were out of stock. Bleached cloth also rose by 1 qian, with Queqiao Hui at 12 liang and 5 qian, Ding Fu Jun at 11 liang and 9 qian, and Fushou Sanxing at 11 liang and 2 qian, 5 fen. Western goods are very difficult to find.

Coal: Two White Coals Suddenly Soared

Mark and Haifeng

Mark white coal and Shaofeng white coal both suddenly soared yesterday, with each ton rising from 19 liang and 5 qian to over 25 liang. An investigation found that this kind of price increase has never happened before. Moreover, the market prices for Hongqi coal and Shanxi coal have not changed. The reason for the sudden price increase is that the white coal comes from French Annam, and now the French exchange rate is high, so the foreign company's prices are expensive. In addition, there have been no arrivals here for more than a month, and the inventory of various merchants is about to run out.
