Japanese Dispatch: Fish demand is healthy, and supply to Dongyang is sought after, with prices for various grades rising by 5 yuan.

Book Review

Municipal Administration Essentials

— South Gentleman

Written by Bai Dunyong

In today's increasingly complex social situation, in order to ensure that people live in an orderly manner, the government must pay special attention to the municipal administration of large cities. A large city has a considerable population. What is important in city life is a new habit, namely "strict discipline, systematic organization, and proactive work." This new habit should be established first, and then the improvement of municipal administration will be easier to promote.

In ancient times, markets were held at midday, and people exchanged goods for goods. Their daily necessities were obtained in this way. Therefore, the center of economic activity gradually became Chengdu and cities. Mencius said, "When King Tai resided in Qi, those who followed him were as if they were returning to the market." This statement is worth pondering. The Zhou Rituals established the court in front and the market in the back, one as the political center and the other as the economic center. These two were the elements that constituted a city. The "market" in ancient times is what is now called the "market" of municipal administration. Although this is the origin of its evolution, the importance of municipal administration can be seen from this. For thousands of years, there has only been the management of marketplaces and no urban planning, which is an undeniable fact. Until modern times, the government and the people have paid considerable attention to municipal administration. Many monographs on municipal administration have also been published. This book, "Municipal Administration Essentials," is characterized by its consideration of folk customs. Its arguments are based on the national conditions of our country and are worthy of the attention of those who study municipal administration.

The first part, "The Evolution of Municipal Systems in Our Country," and the first chapter, "The Municipal System of the Zhou Dynasty," describe the early beginnings of municipal administration in our country. Emperor Yan Shennong held markets at midday, which was the beginning of municipal administration in our country. By the early Zhou Dynasty, it gradually became prosperous. This is described in detail in the "Market Official" chapters of the Zhou Rituals. However, according to the examination, the greatest purpose of the market at that time was trade. Therefore, the officials and their divisions were also focused on this. Although it is not entirely similar to the current urban situation, at that time, when the framework was roughly established, such as municipal administration organs, police, and social undertakings, all had considerable organization, and the management had a clear system, which can be used as a reference for those who speak about municipal administration in the present era. The situation of the markets and shops at that time was quite impressive. The author tries to list them in diagrams to facilitate the reading of researchers.

The second chapter, "The Municipal System of the Tang Dynasty," examines that after the Three Dynasties in our country, the prosperity of Chinese culture and civilization was best represented by the Tang Dynasty. During the Tang Dynasty, it extended to Europe in the west and to the three islands in the east. Therefore, the municipal system of the medieval era in our country also took the Tang Dynasty as the standard. The municipal administration of the Tang Dynasty can be divided into the capital and the prefectures, states, and counties. The author, in view of this, divides it into two sections to describe it. (1) The organization of municipal administration in the capital. The responsibilities of the municipal administration officials in the Tang Dynasty were divided among four officials. A, the Left and Right Golden Guard, similar to the Golden Guard of the Han Dynasty, the Nine Gates Admiral of the Qing Dynasty, and the former Beijing Police Department. B, the Left and Right Street Envoys, similar to the police stations. C, the Director of the Capital Market Office, was an official in charge of municipal administration, similar to the former Municipal Administration Supervisor. D, the Magistrates of Chang'an and Wannian Counties, similar to the magistrates of Daxing and Wanping Counties in the late Qing Dynasty. As for their management of municipal affairs, each differed according to their different powers. Therefore, the scope and nature were also different. The important matters were roughly divided into seven categories: 1. Matters concerning public safety; 2. Matters concerning social undertakings; 3. Matters concerning sanitation; 4. Matters concerning urban planning; 5. Matters concerning public works; 6. Matters concerning parks; 7. Matters concerning finance. Although the names are different, their duties and the responsibilities of modern management are also similar. Therefore, this research work is necessary for modern research on municipal administration to understand. (2) The organization of municipal administration in the prefectures, states, and counties. This was established because the Tang Dynasty established its capital, and although it was not the seat of the state or county, markets could not be set up. However, if markets were to be set up, there were two restrictions. First, the number of households must be more than three thousand. Second, it must be the location of the state or county government. If the population was not more than three households, and markets were to be set up, there must be special circumstances before they could be submitted to the central government for establishment. As for the scope of municipal administration, it was still the same as the prefecture and state, similar to the capital. From this, we can understand that the scale of municipal administration in the Tang Dynasty can be said to be fully prepared. Its advantages can be divided into three: A. Organized; B. Unified administrative power; C. Uniform regulations for undertakings. However, when it comes to the culture of our country, we must refer to the Three Dynasties when it comes to ancient times, and the Zhou Dynasty was the most prosperous of the Three Dynasties. When it comes to the medieval era, the Tang Dynasty was the model. Although the municipal administration of other dynasties is not without reference, it was undoubtedly dominated by the Zhou and Tang Dynasties. This chapter describes the municipal systems of ancient and medieval times, limited to the Zhou and Tang Dynasties, and is sufficient to be used as a reference for the background of municipal administration, although it is research, it is also used as an aid to polishing jade. Those who study municipal systems in our country today cannot ignore this.

The third chapter, "The Municipal System of the Republic of China," is a detailed discussion of the evolution of modern municipal administration. It first describes the changes in the municipal system of Peiping, then the changes in the municipal system of Guangzhou. After the National Government promulgated the "Special Municipality Organization Law" in July of the seventeenth year, Guangzhou also followed the promulgated regulations and was changed to a special municipality. Its system is detailed in the "Special Municipality Organization Law" at the end of this book. After the establishment of Guangzhou, the atmosphere of municipal administration gradually opened up. After the establishment of the National Government, it was determined to rectify municipal administration. The rise of municipal administration was even more vigorous. Up to now, it is also focusing on the local autonomy of the city. The author compiled a detailed chart comparing the "City Organization Regulations" promulgated by the National Government and the "Guangzhou Municipal Provisional Regulations" to provide a shortcut for those who are interested in the evolution of the municipal system.

The second part is "An Overview of the Police." The first chapter, "The Authority of the Police," states that the police system in our country was created in the Zhou Dynasty, with "field lodges" governing the countryside and "Sibaosi" governing the market, so the law was excellent for maintaining order and tranquility. From the Han and Tang Dynasties to modern times, the ancient meaning has been lost. Those who speak of police affairs have instead taken the legal systems of the West as the standard. After the culture fell behind, it is a pity. In May of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, the Legislative Yuan passed the "City Organization Law." The municipal government established four bureaus: 1. Social Bureau, 2. Public Safety Bureau, 3. Finance Bureau, 4. Public Works Bureau. It also stipulates that the municipal government may, with the approval of the higher-level authorities, separately add Education Bureau, Health Bureau, Land Bureau, Public Utilities Bureau, and Port Affairs Bureau when necessary. The responsibilities of the Public Safety Bureau are specified as four categories: A. Public safety matters; B. Fire protection matters; C. Public health matters; D. Establishment and banning of hospitals, vegetable markets, slaughterhouses, and public entertainment venues. This is nothing more than "maintaining law and order," which is the duty of the police, and the duty of the police. Since this is clear, the author discusses it in more detail in the second chapter, "The Organization of the Police." The police organization is unified throughout the country, which is now called the Public Safety Bureau, such as the Traffic Police Team, which manages street traffic, the Security Team, which assists the districts and is prepared for dispatch, the Detective Team, which investigates thieves and bandits, and the Fire Brigade, which extinguishes fires. These are all internal organizations of the Public Safety Bureau, so one can know a glimpse of it. The third chapter, "Using People," says, "The key to governance is in obtaining people." The difficulty of police administration lies especially in obtaining people. If the organization is proper, if there are no suitable talents to fill it, it will be difficult to establish a good tree and achieve good results. From the director to the patrolmen, all are part of the police organism. If one part is improper, it affects the whole. Therefore, the use of police personnel is of great importance. Here, the author discusses them separately. In terms of personnel, such as the director, the police, and the patrolmen, such as the bicycle team, the car team, the uniforms, the rations, the women police, and comparing the police systems of various countries, it is a strength of this book.

The third part, "Municipal Administration and Citizens' Entertainment," discusses the modification and celebration of festivals from the perspective of love of liveliness and outlook on life, and has a detailed description of Chinese folk customs, which is the valuable part of this chapter. The end of the chapter contains ten appendices, which are especially useful for the reference of municipal administration researchers.

The current government pays much attention to municipal administration, such as the utilization and preservation of ancient buildings, and the training of various police forces, which are all attracting the attention of the people of the country. The increasing number of municipal administrations cannot be said to be the progress of the past ten years. However, there are very few books and publications on the evolution of municipal administration in our country, as well as laws and regulations. Now, this book by Bai Jun is indeed valuable. However, the first priority in reforming municipal administration today is to create citizens, and to gradually implement citizens' participation in politics, because good citizens can also create good municipal administration. This is the most important thing in reforming municipal administration today. Although Bai Jun's book does not pay attention to this point, it is indeed a special insight to examine the municipal system of ancient times. As for other advantages, I will not list them one by one.

Critical Essays on European and American Literature

— South Gentleman

Written by Kushi Shiroishi Village, Translated by Summer Record Banana

With the rise of new culture, European and American literature took the lead in the new literary world. In recent years, Japanese literature has bloomed with strange and exotic flowers, which is worthy of pride in countries with backward cultures. However, their general literary researchers still do not neglect European and American literature, seeking the true essence of its value. The rapid advancement of Japanese new culture has a momentum to surpass the former, which is also due to this reason of not being complacent.

Kushi Shiroishi Village, a strong figure in the Japanese literary world, has a deep impression in the minds of modern Chinese readers. His literary theory books with world value, such as "Symbols of Suffering," "Ten Lectures on Modern Literature," and "Out of the Ivory Tower," have become books that must be read by literary researchers. For example, the book "Ten Lectures on Modern Literature" has made many contributions to European literary trends, because such books are not easy to see in the European literary world. The author uses this kind of historical research perspective to judge European and American literature, which is of course very precise and correct. At the same time, we feel that reading ordinary literary reviews often lacks the purpose of reading because these kinds of specialized works have dry and boring content. Some are just some rigid lecture-style materials. It's like a teacher putting on a stern face in the classroom and lecturing on a rigid book, and the students below are just dozing off, without arousing the enthusiasm of the listeners. Kushi Shiroishi Village's literary monographs, however, break this rigid lecture-style category and completely pay attention to interesting narratives, which is its greatness.

This "Critical Essays on European and American Literature" also has this way, and it is even more interesting, making us feel like reading a beautiful creation, but its characteristics and themes belong to literary theory. The first chapter, "Left Foot Amputation," at first we read it, the impression we got was that it was a beautiful narrative essay. At the beginning of the text, he wrote like this: "At the end of March, I wanted to travel to the other side of the sea, and wanted to move my family to Tokyo. When I was busy with various preparations, I accidentally suffered a slight wound on my left foot, which became the cause, swelling terribly and starting to hurt. The fever was also very high, and I couldn't even walk while enduring it. My own foot, already like an enemy, where is the demon nesting? With further determination, I decided to cut it off. While groaning in bed, I thought to myself, in the past, the great master Deng, because his feet were not complete, could not sit properly during Zen meditation, so he sometimes shouted "This ghost foot," and broke it off stiffly. It healed like this and finally died. What a happy monk! I admired it like this. I have felt interesting since I read this story in some book, and I still remember it. Just this little injury, I can't stand it, I'm ashamed of the great master Deng, I thought like this... Cut off one foot, support two crutches, and be able to barely walk to Tokyo." Although the following is still narrated like a story, it gradually tends to the center of literary theory, such as "Hospital life, it can't become a poem after all, it is a kind of boring and annoying thing, especially a work with a surgical operation like mine as the subject," this still contains a strong interest, but the title of this chapter is "Left Foot Amputation," and at the end, we are told the medicine of this stuffy gourd.

"At first there were four feet, in the middle there were two feet, and finally there were three. What is the thing that is stronger the fewer the number of feet?"

"The readers all know that this is the Sphinx riddle in Greece. Those who can't solve this riddle will lose their lives. King Yipus replied beautifully that it was "man." When an infant, he crawls on four feet, and when he is old, he adds a cane to his two feet to become three. In middle age, he has only two, which is the strongest. But like me, with one foot, I didn't say anything. If you say that the fewer the number of feet, the stronger, one foot must be stronger than ordinary people. This is the stronger one that even the Sphinx's riddle doesn't have. If human beings evolve one step further, one foot is enough. It is named Superman. Really, from the perspective of a Superman like me, ordinary and ordinary people with two feet are very ugly and extremely undignified weaklings."

This kind of literary discussion can be said to be pioneering a new path, and it can be used as a reference for literary researchers to create literary theories, which is indeed an unspeakable fact.

The second chapter, "Literary Scholars and Politicians," is a more important commentator, and it can also be said to be a "critique of life" in literature. The discussion is very insightful and full of national thought. It says that literature will join hands with politics, and indicates a way forward for those who study literature, as said at the end of the chapter,

"In order to build a national life with roots, and to create a national life for politics based on true culturalism and humanism, politicians and literary scholars must approach each other. I believe that the day will soon come when there will be a more meaningful and close relationship between the two parties."

Of course, writing literary works is like a balloon that is difficult to open the ground, which is not very reliable. At the same time, it is not necessary to deal with political and social problems directly in his works. However, for these problems, having a single eye, being able to criticize and understand the preparation, as a critic of life, literary scholars cannot be taken lightly. Regarding this, the author also narrates very clearly in this article. When young people who love literature are wandering on a fork in the road, this kind of discussion containing correct thoughts is really a bright light in the dark night. Moreover, the author makes a serious critique of European and American literature, giving beginners many meaningful common sense in literature.

The third chapter, "New Stars in Irish Literature," is to make a concrete and great view of all the excellent things and matters in the European artistic garden, and to introduce the most excellent new writers of Irish drama to the world, which is even more valuable. For example, the one-act plays, in recent years, the works of Lord Danseni, who has overwhelmed the names of Shazhi and Xinggu, because of its performances, in the American artistic garden, he was initially recognized for his true value. Irish drama has occupied a position in the world literary world, which is described in great detail here, and is a great modern drama theory.

The fourth chapter, "Jack London's Novels," he is now known as a first-class writer in the American literary world, and occupies a unique position in the English novel world. However, few people systematically introduce this writer's novels, such as the famous works "The Call of the Wild" and "White Fang," which write about human stories. The author has precise reviews of these here, and his writing style is like writing a novel, as if we are reading Jack London's novels.

Other such as "Game Theory," "American New Theater Troupe," "Literary Communication," two chapters, (1) English and German Academic Style, (2) Reminiscences of Yizhagalai (J, Echegary), "The Revival of Silent Drama," "European War and Overseas Literature," "American University" and other discussions are all very valuable works. Although the text belongs to the category of commentary, we can also treat it as literary thought and literary theory, and there is nothing wrong with it. In each chapter, it is also full of strong interest, which is very convenient for beginners to read. After this book came out, the kind of rigid lecture-style literary works were broken, and this alone is enough to measure its new value.

Summer Gentleman's translation is very smooth and fits the taste of our country's readers very well.

Engineering Construction Summary (9)

— Zhang Yanxiang

"The Evolution and Equipment of Dalian Port", Written by Li Shutian, Gao Xiehe, North China Water Conservancy Monthly, Volume 3, Issue 8, August 1930, Pages 1-14, Publisher: North China Water Conservancy Committee, 11 Wuma Road, Italian Concession, Tianjin.

Although Dalian Port is operated by Japan, it is still within the territory of our country. The people of our country must know its equipment situation, and it can also be used as a reference for opening up other ports. The total construction cost of Dalian Port to date has reached 72 million yuan. It was initially leased and operated by Russia. After the Russo-Japanese War, it was operated by the South Manchurian Railway Company since the 33rd year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty. The port equipment includes (1) Navigation equipment, such as radio stations, radio compass stations, lighthouses, and fog warning signals, (2) Marine equipment, with wave-breaking dikes on the northeast, west, and three sides, with a total length of 13,136 feet, wharves with a total length of 16,294 feet, and a water depth of 24 to 40 feet. Large ships of 20,000 tons can also berth freely. The wharves are more than 400 feet wide. There are also oil storage tanks and erected iron pipes, a special pier for loading and unloading oil, and a special coal-loading machine for loading coal, (3) 15 transfer barges and ice-breaking barges, (4) Marine transportation equipment, three coal-supplying ships, five marine cranes (one 50 tons), two water-supplying ships, (5) Land equipment, 21 warehouses, ship water supply faucets, each wharf has cranes, a total of 50, mostly electric, from 2 tons to 45 tons, 70 miles of railways, 15 locomotives, 200 freight cars, 58 cars, (6) Auxiliary equipment, a seven-story building for offices, etc., connecting transportation for cars and ships, cold storage, dry dock 440 feet long, and port construction workshops, etc. It can be seen that the construction of a seaport has a myriad of details, its scope is extremely large, and it is not an instant success.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) The pictures are limited to the latest works of new domestic and foreign writers and attached pictures related to the text.

(3) Texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) The text of each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

Youth Garden

Performances by the Central Public Theater Society

— Du Shu

The first public performance of the Central Public Theater Society is now a thing of the past.

Beforehand, everyone anticipated that they would not have a good outcome, because although they had rehearsed several times, they did not seem to have a firm grasp of the script. Furthermore, there had been special accidents among the actors, and they had suffered various setbacks. People who sympathized with and cared about them were worried for them. However, unexpectedly, they achieved final success. In the chaotic situation where the audience filled the entire theater, they were able to maintain order very well, so that everyone held their breath and listened to their testimonies. We can imagine how successful they were.

Their unexpected success made many people happy for them and they received many congratulations.

I would like to record their achievements here, and I hope this record will draw social attention to them. Originally, the school drama movement is still in its nascent stage. That an unopened flower bud can already make people so satisfied shows how much their achievements are worth cherishing.

The play they performed was "Margot," which was adapted and translated from English by playwright Gu Zhongyi. They invited Mr. Gu as the director for this performance. The director understood and appreciated the play, both in its broad strokes and fine details, more than anyone else. Therefore, their success this time was not without reason.

Now let us talk about the story in this play.

Margot is a young and beautiful actress. Her will is very weak, and she often chooses the easiest path in life. She wants to get a lot of money and live a false and extravagant life. On the other hand, she also wants to find someone who truly loves her and be happy. Because of this, she creates this tragedy. In this public performance, the role of Margot was played by Ms. Zhang Zhaohua, a female member of their society. Ms. Zhang is a top student at the school, lively and innocent, and her Mandarin is particularly fluent. However, her personality is not very compatible with Margot's. In advance, the general public felt that she was not very suitable, because it seemed that her expressions could only be used in comedies, and not in tragedies, and her attitude did not seem very similar. However, these were entirely the concerns of ordinary people. In the play, she achieved unimaginable success. From beginning to end, she remained very calm and made the whole play very tense. Her expressions of tenderness and strength were used very cleverly. Moreover, her clear speech made the audience listen intently. In the last few scenes, she seemed to be so excited that she forgot herself. In the sad scenes, she simply moved several soft-hearted female audience members to tears. She was indeed the greatest contributor to the success of this public performance. From now on, she will be even more admired by many young people.

The second character to appear was Bai Senqing, a wealthy businessman who is Margot's lover and her financial provider. They found a most suitable actor, Mr. Ouyang Xin, to play this role. Mr. Ouyang has more stage experience and seems to be closer to drama. With his tall stature and loud voice, he made this role vivid and appropriate. He played the bad behavior of the character in the play, but won the sympathy of the audience. He made people laugh, made people excited, and made people unconsciously nervous and afraid. His performance was rare.

Now, let's talk about Margot's lover, the young journalist Ma Ziying. This role was played by the young and energetic Mr. Zhang Liangyi. Mr. Zhang's righteous demeanor was played just right, with no flaws to be found. Mr. Zhang is from Sichuan, and his speech inevitably has a Sichuan accent, so some people were very worried about this beforehand. However, he was different as soon as he stepped on the stage. He unexpectedly satisfied people and unexpectedly succeeded.

There is also Margot's girlfriend, Xiao Chunlan, a woman who is also an actress and has fallen. She is the woman who persuades Margot to return to love and money. She is very flirtatious, a boring woman who wears beautiful clothes and accompanies rich people to watch plays and eat. This role was difficult to find in the Central Public Theater Society, because the female students of the Central Public Theater Society are very conservative. However, in order to make the play successful, a female member, Ms. Zhu Qin, bravely took on the role without hesitation. In the play, she fearlessly displayed her artistic talent. She gave the play another kind of scene. Naturally, she was also successful.

In the middle, Mr. Fan Zhenbang played Qin Jiaotian, an old actor in the play, which was also very rare. His mature, steady, and worldly-wise appearance matched the character's personality. In the two scenes before and after, one sad and one happy, he performed as if he were two different people. We know how cultivated he is in art.

There is also Ms. Wang Hualian, who played the best role of all. In the play, she played Margot's nanny, Gui Ma. Her comical appearance made everyone couldn't help but laugh. However, she, like the movie star Pascale, was not afraid of others laughing so hard that they lost their teeth or their stomachs hurt. She still had an iron face and did her own thing. Someone who does not have a deep understanding and cultivation of drama naturally cannot do this. Therefore, she was naturally valued by ordinary people. Her contribution also made the play very lively, and in the tragic mood, there was a breath of comedy.

All six actors have been mentioned a little. I feel sorry for the brevity of this speech. Fortunately, they are all very hardworking. Let me make up for this shortcoming next time.

They were originally going to go to Nanjing this Saturday for a public performance, but for other reasons, and because the members were scattered due to the school's vacation, they had to cancel the trip. Now they have made up their minds to continue working hard. Probably when school starts next semester, we can hear the news of their second public performance.

Farewell

— Jian Qiu

Kui, he is an honest young man, and he is also very knowledgeable. When he was eighteen years old, he was my elementary school classmate. In that year, after graduation, because of the poverty of his family, he could not continue his studies.

One day during the summer vacation, when the sun was embracing the earth, people were panting at home, so the road seemed very quiet. Only two or three rickshaw pullers were running barefoot on the fire-like road, and although sweat was pouring down like rain,

In order to see Kui, I endured the scorching sun and walked quickly on the sidewalk. In a moment, I arrived at his home. At this time, he was sitting silently at the table. He turned his head and forced a bitter smile, saying,

"Oh, Zhao, you came in this hot weather."

"I came to see you specially." I sat on the chair next to his table, and then I asked him, "What school are you planning to prepare for next semester?"

"Oh," he sighed, and a sad expression appeared on his face immediately. After a long time, he told me about his family situation. He said that when he was thirteen years old, his father unfortunately died. At that time, the whole family's life depended on his mother's diligent work for others to do some hard things, which was considered to have maintained the family to this day. In these five years, his mother had suffered all kinds of pain because of him, so her body had become very weak. Therefore, in the next semester, he could not have the hope of rising.

After the farewell, time passed quickly day by day. This semester, I was admitted to Nanjing Middle School, but I often thought of Kui. One day, I was pacing alone in the room. The withered weeds outside the window were rustling in the wind, grieving for autumn. Suddenly, Kui came back to my mind again. Oh, I haven't met him for a long time. Who knew that the next morning, his mother would meet me on the way.

"Auntie, where is Kui?" I asked her.

"Kui went to Hankou to do business last month. Didn't he send you a letter?"

I was stunned, looking at her blankly, as if a heavy stone was pressing on my heart.

"Did he send you a letter?" Only when she asked me for the second time did I realize it.

"He didn't send me a letter."

"Then I will tell you his mailing address." At that time, I took out my diary and pencil from my pocket, copied Kui's address, and then hurriedly said goodbye to his mother.

I took a walk on the street, and then returned home listlessly. I sat down on the chair near the window, and for a moment I felt as if I had received a great stimulus. I remembered that in school, all the teachers and students said that he had talent in literature, and his scores in each subject were above average in every semester. However, because of economic difficulties, he could not go to school as he wished. Ah, his promising future was ruined by life.
